Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate

Rukhsah for the Mukrah: Distinguishing Rights of Allah from Rights of Men
Dispute with Shafi'i on rukhsah for compulsion to adultery

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on concession under compulsion and apply the distinction between rights of Allah and rights of men to determine when rukhsah is granted.

Core Idea
Compulsion grants concession only when the act involves rights of men, not purely devotional obligations to Allah.

This passage presents a key usul dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the effect of overwhelming compulsion (ikrah mulji') on the permissibility of committing a prohibited act like adultery. The Hanafi school holds that a concession (rukhsah) is granted when the compulsion involves a threat to life or limb, because the coerced person's protected interest (life) is violated. However, this concession does not extend to acts that are purely rights of Allah, such as abandoning faith or prayer. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the principle of ikrah in fatwa and legal judgment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Locate the phrase 'خلافاً للشافعي' to recognise that the Hanafi position is being contrasted with al-Shafi'i's view on the ruling for a woman compelled to adultery under threat of death or mutilation.
The specific scenario is a man saying 'Are you truly a wife?' implying a claim of marriage under compulsion.
2
Locate the Hanafi proof
Find the phrase 'لأن ذلك تعد من ملحق محترم' (because that is a violation of a protected interest). This is the core talil (reasoning) that establishes the concession.
The protected interest (malhak muhtaram) is the life or bodily integrity of the coerced person.
3
Examine the distinction between rights of Allah and rights of men
The text divides actions into two categories: those pertaining exclusively to Allah (like faith, prayer, fasting) and those involving rights of men (like divorce, sale, and acts affecting lineage). Concession is only granted in the latter category.
The passage states: 'قسم من الله في الإيمان القائم الحمل السقوط؛ لا يرخص فيه' (a section from Allah concerning faith... no concession is granted).
4
Apply the distinction to the case of adultery
Adultery under compulsion involves the right of the coerced person (to preserve life) and also affects lineage (a right of men). Therefore, a concession is granted. However, the concession is limited to overwhelming compulsion (death/mutilation), not mere imprisonment.
The text specifies 'بالقتل أو التقطيع' (by killing or cutting) as the threshold; imprisonment does not suffice.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a Hanafi judge would not punish the woman coerced into adultery under threat of death, whereas a Shafi'i judge might hold her liable for the sin.
This difference stems from the foundational usul principle that rights of men can be subjected to substitution or fall due to necessity, while rights of Allah cannot.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر أن نقول الرجل لامرأة: هل حق كن؟ وهي معروفة النسب وتولد لمثله. وبه أبداً عندنا خلافاً للشافعي. إن الحصيفة في الأكبر مخالفة وفي الأصغر ثبت الحسنة مطلقاً لأنها ثبتت أصلًا من منع اليمين في حق المقر. وأيضاً في حكم القلم لأن التحريم الثابت على العام لوضع يمينه سمنات الكلى الوحدة. إنه حق من حقوقه. ثم قال: إن أكرهت كلاً على الزنا بالقتل أو التقطيع رخص لها في ذلك لأن ذلك تعد من ملحق محترم. ثم قال: نور سائر حقوق الله و الإنساني. ذكر منع الحمل لان نسب الولد فيها لا يستطيع. ولهذا إذا أكرهتها على الزنا بالحبس لا اسـ[؟] تحلالات الكامل يوجد الرخصة فصار العاصر عال خلاف الرجل فصار هذا القسم قسمين: قسم من الله في الإيمان القائم الحمل السقوط؛ لا يرخص فيه لأن الإمام ركن في العقل مصرون احتمال الرخصة بالتبديل ومخلف الرخوة الأداء للضرور. ولما سبق أن أصل الفروع التوحيد والبيان، والأصل في الاعتقاد و الأداء حجبات ركن ختم إليه فصار من المشروع وأساس الدين الاحتلال السقوط والتعدي إلى أن صارفين عريضة العوارض. وما كان من حقوق العباد ومن حسن بعمل السورة قسم اجراء عمل السقوط بصلة لكن دليل السفرة المالم يوجد وجبا المانع باثبات الرخصة والما واجب بصلة.
And he mentioned that a man says to his wife: 'Are you truly a wife?' And she is of known lineage and capable of childbearing. And this is our position always, contrary to al-Shafi'i. Indeed, the decisive [ruling] in the greater [matter] is contradictory, and in the lesser [matter] the good is established absolutely because it is established as a principle from preventing the oath in the right of the confessor. And also in the judgment of the pen because the prohibition established generally upon his oath [has] completeness of the kidneys of the unit. It is a right from his rights. Then he said: If she compels him to adultery by killing or mutilation, a concession is granted for her in that because that is considered a violation of a protected [interest]. Then he said: the light of the rest of the rights of Allah and the human. He mentioned the prevention of pregnancy because the lineage of the child in her cannot be [established]. And for this, if she compels him to adultery by imprisonment, no complete dissolution [؟] exists, but the concession exists, so the coerced [؟] becomes like the free man in contradiction. So this section became two sections: a section from Allah concerning faith, established pregnancy and fall [of rights]; no concession is granted in it because the imam is a pillar in the intellect, they accept the possibility of concession by substitution and the remainder of the ease of performance due to necessity. And because the origin of the branches is tawhid and clarification, and the origin in belief and performance is obligations, a pillar concluded to it, so it became from the legislated and the foundation of the religion: the fall and the transgression [؟] until that the obstacles are wide. And whatever was from the rights of servants and from good with the chapter of work, a section of executing work of fall is connected but the proof of the journey is not found and the preventer is to establish the concession and what is obligatory is connected.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is a dispute with al-Shafi'i concerning the effect of compulsion (ikrah) on the validity of actions and the granting of concessions (rukhsah). The author argues that when a person is compelled to commit adultery under threat of death or mutilation, a concession is granted because the act is considered a violation of a protected interest (i.e., the victim's life). However, the concession does not extend to matters purely related to rights of Allah, such as the foundation of faith (iman), because those are pillars of belief that cannot be substituted. The passage divides the rulings into two sections: those belonging to Allah (like faith and worship) where no concession is allowed through substitution or fall, and those belonging to the rights of servants (like divorce or sales) where concession can apply due to necessity. The Hanafi position is presented as contrary to al-Shafi'i, who likely holds a different view on the scope of rukhsah for the mukrah. The text also touches on the idea that the origin (asl) of the branches of fiqh is tawhid (monotheism) and clarification (bayan), emphasizing that the fundamental principles of religion are not subject to fall or transgression.

Key Terms
إكراه (ikrah): Compulsion that negates free will, specifically through threats of death or severe bodily harm.
رخصة (rukhsah): A concession granted to the mukrah allowing commission of a normally prohibited act due to necessity.
حق الله (haqq Allah): A right belonging solely to Allah, such as the obligation of faith, prayer, and fasting; these cannot be substituted or dropped due to compulsion.
حق العبد (haqq al-'abd): A right belonging to a human being, such as financial claims or personal status matters like divorce and marriage; these can be affected by compulsion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, when is a concession (rukhsah) granted for committing adultery under compulsion (ikrah)?
A) Only when the threat is of death or dismemberment
B) Only when the threat is of imprisonment
C) Always, as long as there is any compulsion
D) Never, because adultery is a sin even when compelled

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school grants a concession for adultery under overwhelming compulsion (death/mutilation) because it involves a protected interest and falls under rights of men, not purely rights of Allah.

The Hanafi View That Command Requires a Verbal Form
Dispute on whether command is necessarily verbal or can be conveyed by actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on the nature of command (amr), evaluate the opposing evidence, and apply the usul principle that actions alone do not create obligation.

Core Idea
A command is only binding when expressed in a specific verbal form; actions alone do not create obligation.

In this passage, the Hanafi school argues that command (al-amr) is necessarily expressed by a verbal form, not by actions. Some Maliki and Shafi'i scholars disagree, claiming the Prophet's actions are equally obligating. This lesson examines the evidence and reasoning behind the Hanafi position, highlighting the linguistic and prophetic support for requiring a clear verbal command.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Read the passage and state the Hanafi position (that command has a specific verbal form) and the opposing position (that actions also constitute command).
2
Analyze the opposing proof
Examine the Quranic verse (11:97) and hadith ("Pray as you see me praying") used by opponents. Note how they interpret these to support their view.
The opponents take the word 'amr' in the verse as meaning 'action'.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Study the Hanafi linguistic argument: expressions are established for meanings; actions are ambiguous. Also consider the prophetic incidents (removing sandals, continuous fasting) where the Prophet disapproved of imitation.
The Hanafis argue that if actions were commands, the Prophet would not have objected to being followed.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: Hanafis do not consider following the Prophet's action obligatory without a verbal command; others do.
5
Recognize the mufta bihi
The text clearly prefers the Hanafi position; note that this is the relied-upon view within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الأمر
فإن المراد بالأمر يختص بصيغة لازمة عندنا.
ومن الناس من قال : ليس للمراد بالأمر صيغة لازمة.
وحاصل ذلك : أن أفعال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عندهم موجِبَةٌ، وهو قول بعض أصحاب مالك والشافعي رحمهم الله.
كالأمر، واحتجوا بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا أَمْرُ فِرْعَوْنَ بِرَشِيد﴾ [هود: 97] : أي فعله، ولو لم يكن الأمر مستفاداً بالفعل: لما سُمِّي به.
وقال النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام: «صلوا كما رأيتموني أصلي»، فجَعَلَ المتابعة لازمة.
واحتج أصحابنا رحمهم الله بأن العبارات إنما وضعت دلالات على المعاني المقصودة، ولا يجوز قصور العبارات عن المقاصد والمعاني. وقد وجدنا كل مقاصد الفعل، مثلُ الماضي والحال والاستقبال مختصةً بعبارات وضعت لها، فالمقصود بالأمر كذلك أن يكون مختصاً يجب بالعبارة، وهذا المقصود من أعظم المقاصد، فهو بذلك أولى.
وإذا ثبت أصل الموضوع كان حقيقةً، فتكون لازمةً إلا بدليل ألا يُرى أن أسماء الحقائق لا تسقط عن مسمياتها أبداً، وأما المجاز فيصح نفيه. يقال للأب الأقرب أب، لا ينتفي عنه بحال، ويسمى الجد : أباً، ويصح نفيه.
ثم ههنا صح أن يقال : إن فلاناً لم يأمر اليوم بشيء مع كثرة أفعاله، وإذا تكلم بعبارة الأمر : لم يستقم نفيه.
وقد قال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم حين خلع نعليه، فخلع الناس نعالهم منكراً عليهم : ما لكم خلعتُم نعالكم ؟ ).
وأنكر عليهم الموافقة في وصال الصوم، فقال: «إني أبيتُ يُطعمني ربي ويسقيني».
Chapter of Command
Indeed, the intended meaning of 'command' is specific to a necessary verbal form according to us. Some people said: The intended meaning of command does not have a necessary verbal form. The gist of that is that the actions of the Prophet, peace be upon him, according to them are obligating, and that is the saying of some followers of Malik and al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on them. Like the command, and they argued with His saying the Exalted: 'And the command of Pharaoh was not right' [Hud 11:97]: i.e., his action, and if command were not understood from action, it would not be called by it. And the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Pray as you see me praying,' so he made following obligatory. And our companions, may Allah have mercy on them, argued that expressions are only established as indications of intended meanings, and it is not permissible for expressions to fall short of purposes and meanings. And we have found every purpose of action, such as past, present, and future, specific to expressions established for them. So the intended meaning of command is likewise to be specific, necessarily by expression, and this purpose is among the greatest purposes, so it is more deserving of that. And if the origin of the subject is established, it is a reality, so it is necessary unless by evidence. Do you not see that names of realities never depart from their named entities, while metaphor may be negated. It is said: The nearest father is 'father', it is not negated from him at all, and the grandfather is called 'father', and it may be negated. Then here, it is correct to say: So-and-so did not give any command today despite many actions, but if he spoke with the expression of command, its negation is not proper. And the Prophet, peace be upon him, said when he removed his sandals and the people removed their sandals, disapproving of them: 'Why did you remove your sandals?' And he disapproved of their agreement in continuous fasting, saying: 'Indeed I spend the night while my Lord feeds me and gives me drink.'
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute about the nature of command (al-amr) in Islamic jurisprudence. The Hanafi position (summarized as 'at our end') is that command is specifically indicated by a necessary verbal form (sigha laazima). Opponents, including some Maliki and Shafi'i scholars, argue that the Prophet's actions are also obligating, like verbal commands. They cite Quran 11:97 where 'amr' is interpreted as 'action', and the hadith 'Pray as you see me praying' to support the idea that actions imply obligation. The Hanafi response is that language is specifically established to convey meanings; actions cannot reliably convey specific legal categories like obligation because they are ambiguous. The passage uses an analogy: just as past, present, and future have specific verbal forms, so does command. If action could constitute command, one could not say 'today he did not command anything' despite many actions, but one can say that. The Prophet's disapproval of companions imitating his actions (removing sandals during prayer, continuous fasting) shows that actions alone do not convey obligation; otherwise, he would have praised them. Thus, the Hanafi school holds that command must be verbal, and imitation of the Prophet's actions only becomes required if there is a verbal command or clear evidence that it is obligatory.

Key Terms
الأمر (al-amr): In this passage, 'amr' is discussed as a legal command; the Hanafi position is that it must be expressed verbally, not through action.
صيغة لازمة (sigha laazima): A necessary verbal form that is the exclusive indicator of command.
أفعال النبي (af'al al-nabiy): Actions of the Prophet; the dispute is whether they are binding (mujiba) like commands.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the primary indicator of a command?
A) The action of the Prophet
B) A specific verbal form
C) The consensus of scholars
D) The general good of the community

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that command is specifically indicated by a verbal form (sigha laazima), and the Prophet's actions are not inherently obligating without such a form.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

The Basis of Qada: Obligated by Text or Cause?
Presents a dispute among mashayikh about the basis for qada.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two positions in the Hanafi dispute on the basis of qada and apply the majority position to derive rulings for missed acts by analogy.

Core Idea
Qada is obligated by the same cause as ada, not by a separate text.

In this passage from Usul al-Bazdawi, the author clarifies the terms 'ada' and 'qada' and then presents a dispute among the early Hanafi scholars (mashayikh) regarding what makes qada obligatory. One group argues that a specific textual command is needed for each missed act, while the majority holds that the original cause (sabab) that made the act obligatory in its time also obligates its makeup. Understanding this dispute is crucial for deriving rulings on missed acts of worship by analogy.

Guided Path
1
Understand the terms Ada and Qada
Start by grasping the linguistic nuance: 'ada' implies thoroughness and delivery of the exact duty, while 'qada' is a broader term meaning to perfect something. This sets the stage for the dispute.
The author uses the example of the wolf's cunning to illustrate the intensity of 'ada'.
2
Identify the two positions on Qada
Some mashayikh say qada requires a specific text (nass maqsud) because acts of worship are defined by their times. The majority say qada is obligated by the same cause (sabab) as ada, using textual and rational proofs.
Note which group is the majority; this will be the relied-upon Hanafi position.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The author cites the Quranic verse on fasting (2:184) and the hadith on making up missed prayer. Then explains the rational: the missed obligation becomes a liability, and since one can perform supererogatory acts of its type, he can use them to fulfill the debt.
The virtue of the time is lost, but the obligation remains.
4
Apply the principle via Qiyas
The author shows that this principle extends to other missed acts, such as prayers missed during Tashriq (made up without takbir) and failed i'tikaf vows (must be made up in another month).
These are practical consequences of adopting the majority view.
5
Summarize the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical difference between the two positions is that the minority would require a new text for each missed act, while the majority can derive the ruling by qiyas. This affects rulings like the absence of takbir in missed Tashriq prayers.
The Hanafi school relies on the majority position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قضاء؛ لأن القضاء لفظ متّسع.
وقد يُستعمل الأداء في القضاء مقيَّداً؛ إلا أن للأداء خصوصاً بتسليم نفس الواجب وعينه ؛ لأن مرجع العبارة إلى الاستقصاء، وشدة الرعاية، كما قيل في الثلاثي منه : الذئب يأدو للغزال يأكله أي يحتال ويتكلف فيَختله.
وأما القضاء : فإحكام الشيء نفسه لا ينبيء عن شدة الرعاية.
:
واختلف المشايخ رحمهم الله في القضاء أيجب بنص مقصود، أم بالسبب الذي يوجب الأداء؟
فقال بعضُهم : بنص مقصود ؛ لأن القُربة عُرفت قُربةً بوقتها، وإذا فاتت عن وقتها : فلا يعرف لها مثل إلا بالنص المقصود، وكيف يكون مثلاً
لها بالقياس وقد ذهب وصف فضل الوقت؟
وقال عامتهم : يجب بذلك السبب.
وبيان ذلك : أن الله تعالى أوجب القضاء في الصوم بالنص، فقال تعالى: ﴿فَعِدَّةٌ مِّنْ أَيَّامٍ أُخَرَ ( البقرة / ١٨٤ .
وجاءت السنة بالقضاء في الصلاة، قال النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام مَن نام عن صلاة أو نسيها : فليصلها إذا ذَكَرَها ، فإن ذلك وقتها » (۱).
فقلنا نحن وجب القضاء في هذا بالنص، وهو معقول، فإن الأداء كان فرضاً في الوقت فإذا فات كان مضموناً، وهو قادر على تسليم مثله من عنده ؛ لكون النفل مشروعاً له من جنسه، أمر بصرف ما له بصرف ما لَه إلى ما
عليه، وسقط فضل الوقت إلى غير مثل وإلى غير ضمان، إلا بالإثم إن كان عامداً؛ للعجز.
فإذا عُقل هذا وجب القياس به في قضاء المنذورات المتعينة من الصلاة والصيام والاعتكاف
وهذا أقيس وأشبه بمسائل أصحابنا رحمهم الله ، ولهذا قلنا في صلاة فاتت عن أيام التشريق وجب قضاؤها بلا تكبير ؛ لأنه لا تكبير عنده في سائر الأيام، ثم لم يسقط ما قَدَرَ عليه بهذا العذر.
ويتفرع من هذا الأصل مسألة النذر بالاعتكاف في شهر رمضان إذا
صامه ولم يعتكفه أنه يقضي اعتكافه ولا يجزئ في شهر رمضان آخر.
،
أحدكم عن الصلاة، أو غفل عنها : فليصلها إذا ذكرها، فإن الله تعالى يقول: ﴿وَأَقِمِ الصَّلَوةَ لِذِكْرِي . وفي رواية: «مَن نسي صلاةً فليصلها إذا ذكرها، لا كفارة لها إلا ذلك».
أخرج الأولى مسلم، والثانية متفق عليها.
وعن أبي قتادة قال : ذكروا للنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم نومهم عن الصلاة، فقال: إنه ليس في النوم تفريط، إنما التفريط في اليقظة، فإذا نسي أحدكم صلاة، أو نام
عنها فليصلها إذا ذكرها ، رواه النسائي والترمذي، وصححه.
وعن أبي هريرة أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «مَن نسي صلاةً: فوقتُها إذا ذكرها. رواه الطبراني في الوسط وفيه حفص بن عمر: ضعيف.
Judicial decree because the word 'qada' is broad. And sometimes 'ada' is used for 'qada' in a restricted sense; however 'ada' has specificity in delivering the exact same obligation and its essence, because the import of the expression is thoroughness and intense care, as is said in its triliteral form: the wolf 'ya'du' (creeps up) to the gazelle to eat it, meaning it uses cunning and effort to deceive it. As for 'qada': it is to perfect the thing itself, not indicating intense care. The mashayikh differed concerning qada: is it obligatory by a specific text, or by the cause that necessitates ada? Some said: by a specific text, because an act of worship is known to be worship by its time, and when it leaves its time, its like is not known except by a specific text, and how could it be analogous while the virtue of the time has been lost? The majority said: it is obligatory by that cause. The explanation: Allah obligated qada for fasting by text: 'then a number of other days' (al-Baqarah 2:184). And the Sunnah came with qada for prayer: the Prophet said: 'Whoever sleeps through a prayer or forgets it, let him pray it when he remembers, for that is its time.' (1). Then we said: qada in this case is obligated by text, and it is rational: ada was obligatory in time, and when it is missed it becomes a liability, and he is able to deliver its like from his own [voluntary acts] because supererogatory acts of its type are legislated for him; he is commanded to redirect what he has to what is owed, and the virtue of the time falls away without a like and without liability, except for sin if he was intentional, due to inability. When this is understood, analogy becomes necessary for qada of determinate vows of prayer, fasting, and i'tikaf. This is more analogous and closer to the issues of our companions. For this reason we said regarding a prayer missed during the days of Tashriq: it must be made up without takbir, because there is no takbir on those days elsewhere, and then what he was able to do is not dropped due to this excuse. From this principle branches the issue of vowing i'tikaf in Ramadan: if he fasted and did not perform i'tikaf, he must make up the i'tikaf and it is not sufficient in another Ramadan. One of you about the prayer or is heedless of it: let him pray it when he remembers, for Allah says: 'establish prayer for My remembrance.' And in another narration: 'Whoever forgets a prayer, let him pray it when he remembers; there is no expiation for it except that.' The first was reported by Muslim, the second is agreed upon. From Abu Qatada: they mentioned to the Prophet their sleeping through prayer, and he said: 'There is no negligence in sleep; negligence is only while awake. So if one of you forgets a prayer or sleeps through it, let him pray it when he remembers.' Reported by al-Nasa'i and al-Tirmidhi, and he authenticated it. From Abu Hurayra: the Prophet said: 'Whoever forgets a prayer, its time is when he remembers.' Reported by al-Tabarani in al-Awsat, and it contains Hafs ibn Umar: weak.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Bazdawi begins with a clarification of two key terms: 'ada' (performance on time) and 'qada' (making up after the time). The author notes that 'qada' is a broader term, and 'ada' is sometimes used restrictively for 'qada'. However, 'ada' specifically means delivering the exact obligation with its essence, implying thoroughness and care. The triliteral root 'a-d-a' is illustrated with the wolf's cunning. 'Qada' is simply to perfect the thing itself without such intensity.

The core of the passage is a dispute among the early Hanafi scholars (mashayikh) regarding the basis of qada. One group holds that qada is obligated by a specific textual command (nass maqsud) because acts of worship are known only by their prescribed times; once the time is lost, we cannot know their substitute except by a new text. Analogy (qiyas) would be inadequate because the virtue of the time is gone.

The majority (which includes the relied-upon Hanafi position) holds that qada is obligated by the same cause (sabab) that made ada obligatory. To prove this, the author cites the Quranic verse on fasting (al-Baqarah 2:184) and the hadith about one who sleeps through or forgets a prayer: he should pray it when he remembers. These texts directly command qada, but the Hanafis argue that the underlying rationale is rationally understood: ada was a duty in its time; when it is missed, it becomes a liability (dhimma). Since one is capable of performing its like through supererogatory acts of the same type, he is commanded to divert his voluntary acts to fulfill the missed obligation. The virtue of the time is lost, but the obligation remains.

Based on this rational understanding, the author argues that qada for all missed determinate obligations (like prayed, fasts, and i'tikaf that were vowed) is established by qiyas on the texts mentioned. This is in line with the principles of the Hanafi school. An example is given: a prayer missed during the days of Tashriq (the three days after Eid al-Adha) is made up without the takbirat al-tashriq, because those takbirs are only on those days and are not part of the essential prayer.

Finally, a branch issue: if someone vows to perform i'tikaf in Ramadan but fails to do so, he must make up that i'tikaf in another month; it cannot be done in another Ramadan because that would be a different time and not a make-up of the original vow.

The appended hadiths provide supporting evidence for the ruling on making up missed prayers.

Key Terms
أداء (ada): Performing an obligation within its prescribed time with full care and delivery of the exact duty.
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed obligation after its time has passed. It is a broader term and does not imply the same intensity as ada.
سبب (sabab): The cause or occasion that makes an act obligatory, such as the entrance of prayer time or the occurrence of a sin that requires expiation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi mashayikh, what is the basis for the obligation of qada (making up a missed act)?
A) A specific textual command for each type of act.
B) The same cause (sabab) that made the original ada obligatory.
C) The general principle of preserving acts of worship.
D) Consensus (ijma) of the Companions.

Key Takeaway
Qada is obligated by the same cause that made the original act obligatory, allowing qiyas to extend the ruling to all missed obligatory acts.

Qada' and Ihtiyat for Non-Rational Texts
Defending Hanafi rulings on fidyah and udhiyah via ihtiyat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of ihtiyat to rulings derived from non-rational texts and distinguish between certain and precautionary obligations.

Core Idea
For non-rational texts, obligation is replaced by precautionary action (ihtiyat) when certainty is not possible.

This passage addresses a critical usul question: when a ruling is based on a text whose rationale we do not understand (nass ghayr ma'qul), how do we handle analogous cases or substitutes? The Hanafis use ihtiyat (precaution) to command action without certainty, as seen in the obligations of fidyah for missed prayers and the substitute for udhiyah after its time. You will explore how this principle works and why it differs from a certain ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the non-rational text
Recognize that rulings for ramy al-jimar, standing at 'Arafah, and udhiyah are derived from texts whose 'illah is not known. Therefore, no qiyas can establish a substitute for them.
These are 'ibadat with fixed forms.
2
Recognize the use of ihtiyat for fidyah
The objector asks why fidyah in Salah is obligated by analogy to Sawm without an 'illah. The answer: we are uncertain so we command it as a precaution, hoping for acceptance, not with certainty.
Note the distinction between certainty in Sawm and precaution in Salah.
3
Apply ihtiyat to the udhiyah case
When udhiyah time passes, the original rule for charity (giving value) is applied as a precaution, because the text that transferred the ruling is uncertain.
The substitute does not revert when the original becomes possible again, proving it is not a true substitute.
4
Distinguish the internal ikhtilaf
Muhammad and Abu Yusuf differ on the nature of the transfer from charity to sacrifice (blood only vs. blood and property), but both agree on the final ruling of wajib after the time passes.
This ikhtilaf does not change the operative ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولهذا قلنا إن رمي الجمار لا يُقضى والوقوف بعرفات، والأضحية كذلك. فإن قيل : فإذا ثبت هذا بنص غير معقول، فلم أوجبتم الفدية في الصلاة بلا نص قياساً على الصوم من غير تعليل؟ قلنا : لأن ما ثبت من حكم الفدية عن الصوم يحتمل أن يكون معلولاً، والصلاة نظيرُ الصوم، بل هي أهم منه، لكنا لم نعقل، واحتمل أن لا يكون معلولاً وما لا ندركه لا يلزمنا العمل به، لكنه لما احتمل الوجهين أمرناه بالفدية احتياطاً، فلئن كان مشروعاً: فقد تأدى، وإلا : فليس به بأس. ثم لم نحكم بجوازه مثل ما حكمنا به في الصوم؛ لأنا حكمنا به في الصوم قطعاً، ورَجَوْنا القبول من الله تعالى في الصلاة فضلاً. وقال محمد رحمه الله في «الزيادات» في هذا : يُجزئه إن شاء الله تعالى، كما إذا تطوع به الوارث في الصوم. فإن قيل : فالأضحية لا مثلَ لها، وقد أوجبتُم بعد فوات وقتها التصدق بالعين أو بالقيمة؟ قلنا : لأن التضحية ثبتت قُربةً بالنص، واحتمل أن يكون التصدق بعين الشاة أو بقيمتها أصلاً؛ لأنه هو المشروع في باب المال، كما في سائر الصدقات، إلا أن الشرع نَقَلَ من الأصل إلى التضحية، وهو نقصان في المالية بإراقة الدم عند محمد رحمه الله وبإراقة الدم وإزالة التمول عن الباقي عند أبي يوسف رحمه الله على ما نبين إن شاء الله في مسألة التضحية أيمنع الرجوع في الهبة أم لا؟ فنقل إلى هذا تطييباً للطعام، وتحقيقاً لمعنى العيد بالضيافة، إلا أنه يحتمل أن تكون التضحية أصلاً، فلم يُعتبر هذا الموهوم في معارضة المنصوص المتيقن فإذا فات المتيقن بفوات وقته : وجب العمل بالموهوم مع الاحتمال؛ احتياطاً أيضاً. والدليل على أنه كان بهذا الطريق لا أنه مثل الأضحية : أنه إذا جاء العام القابلُ: لم ينتقل الحكم إلى الأضحية، وهذا وقت يقدر فيه على أداء مثل الأصل، فيجب أن يبطل الخلفُ كما في الفدية، إلا أنه لما ثبت أصلاً من الوجه الذي بينا، وقع الحكم به : لم ينتقض بالشك أيضاً.
And for this reason we said that the throwing of pebbles is not made up, nor the standing at 'Arafah, and likewise the sacrifice. If it is said: Since this is established by a non-rational text, why did you obligate the fidyah in prayer without a text, by analogy to fasting without causal reasoning? We say: Because what is established regarding the ruling of fidyah from fasting may be causally grounded, and prayer is similar to fasting, indeed more important, but we do not understand the cause, and it is possible that it is not causally grounded, and what we do not perceive we are not obliged to act upon, but since it admits two possibilities, we commanded fidyah as a precaution; if it is legislated, then it has been discharged, otherwise there is no harm. Then we did not rule on its validity as we ruled on it in fasting; because we ruled on it in fasting with certainty, and we hope for acceptance from Allah Almighty in prayer as a favor. And Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, said in al-Ziyadat regarding this: It will suffice him if Allah wills, just as if the heir gives it voluntarily in fasting. If it is said: The sacrifice has no equivalent, and you obligated after its time has passed the giving of charity of the animal or its value? We say: Because the sacrifice is established as an act of worship by text, and it is possible that giving charity of the animal itself or its value is the original, because that is legislated in the matter of wealth, as in other charities, except that the Law transferred from the original to the sacrifice, which is a decrease in wealth by shedding blood according to Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, and by shedding blood and removing property from the remainder according to Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, as we will explain, if Allah wills, in the issue of the sacrifice: does it prevent returning a gift or not? It transferred to this for the purpose of making food pleasant and realizing the meaning of the holiday through hospitality, except that it is possible that the sacrifice is the original, so this assumed one is not considered in opposition to the certain text; when the certain is lost by the loss of its time, it becomes necessary to act upon the assumed with possibility, also as a precaution. And the proof that it was by this path, not that it is like the sacrifice, is that when the next year comes, the ruling does not transfer to the sacrifice, and this is a time when one is able to perform something like the original, so the substitute must be invalidated as in the fidyah, except that since it was established originally from the angle we explained, and the ruling was made by it, it is not invalidated by doubt either.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage addresses the usul principle of how rulings based on non-rational texts (nusus ghayr ma'qula) interact with qiyas and ihtiyat. The author begins by stating that ramy al-jimar, standing at 'Arafah, and sacrifice (udhiyah) are not made up if missed, because their rulings are derived from texts that are not rationally understood; thus no qiyas can be applied to establish a substitute. An objector then asks why the Hanafis oblige fidyah in Salah by analogy to Sawm without establishing a common illah. The answer: the fidyah in Sawm might be an illah-based ruling, and Salah is similar; due to uncertainty, they command fidyah as a precaution (ihtiyat), hoping for acceptance. Imam Muhammad adds in al-Ziyadat that it will be accepted if Allah wills. Another objection concerns udhiyah: after its time has passed, why command giving the animal or its value when udhiyah has no substitute? The answer: udhiyah is established as an act of worship by text; the original rule for wealth is to give value, but the Law transferred to slaughter; when the time passes, the precautionary measure is to return to the original, giving the value. The proof that this method is correct is that when the next year comes, the obligation does not revert to udhiyah, unlike if it were a true substitute. The passage also notes a difference between Muhammad and Abu Yusuf in the nature of the transfer from the original.

Key Terms
نص غير معقول (nass ghayr ma'qul): Textual proof whose rationale (illah) is not understood by human reason
فدية (fidyah): Compensation due for omitted acts of worship
احتياط (ihtiyat): Precautionary legal measure taken when the ruling is uncertain
قياس (qiyas): Analogical deduction based on a common cause

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the Hanafis not rule with certainty that the fidyah in salah is valid, unlike in sawm?
A) Because the text for salah is non-rational.
B) Because they followed the same ruling as in sawm with certainty.
C) Because they only hoped for acceptance as a precaution (ihtiyat).
D) Because Abu Hanifa explicitly said so.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi use of ihtiyat allows ruling on cases derived from non-rational texts by precaution, not certainty, distinguishing it from established rulings.

Types of Mithl: Kamil and Qasir in Damages
Explains complete and deficient mithl with examples from marriage, ghasp, and qisas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between al-mithl al-kamil and al-mithl al-qasir, apply the timing rule for value assessment, and evaluate the Hanafi position on disputed cases.

Core Idea
Complete likeness (form and meaning) is the default; deficient likeness (value) becomes due only when the original is impossible, established by court.

In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi classification of compensation into complete and deficient likeness (al-mithl al-kamil wa al-qasir). The passage from al-Bazdawi uses three vivid examples—a wife's slave, usurped food, and retaliation for combined injuries—to illustrate when exact restitution is required and when value substitutes. You will see how the school's principles resolve inter-madhhab and intra-school disagreements.

Guided Path
1
Trace the first example: wife’s slave
Identify why the wife does not own the slave until delivery (it is mithl min wajh) and why the husband’s acts (freeing, selling) are valid. This establishes the default of mithl.
The slave is considered a mithli item because it can be valued, but not a perfect mithl.
2
Analyze the ghasp dispute
Compare the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on feeding the owner without knowledge. The Hanafi view treats it as valid performance (ada’) because the same property reached the owner; the Shafi'i view sees it as deception (ghurur).
This dispute hinges on whether the intention matters when the property physically returns.
3
Define al-mithl al-kamil and al-mithl al-qasir
Extract the definitions: complete mithl matches in form and meaning (like returning the same item); deficient mithl is value when the exact item is unavailable or has no mithl.
The complete mithl is the original (asl) in guarantees.
4
Examine the qisas example
Note the difference between Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Sahibayn) on cutting a hand then killing. Abu Hanifa allows both as complete mithl; the companions argue killing alone suffices because it subsumes the cut.
This shows how form and meaning can diverge: cutting then killing is complete in form but may be redundant in meaning.
5
Derive the timing rule
Understand why value (deficient mithl) is only assessed on the day of litigation according to Abu Hanifa: the possibility of the original mithl remains until the judge rules it unavailable.
This is a principle of caution: avoid substituting value while the original might still be deliverable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولهذا قلنا: إنه لا يعتق عليها قبل القبض حتى يسلمه إليها، أو يُقضى به لها ؛ لأنه مثل من وجه، فلا تملك إلا بالتسليم. ولهذا قلنا : إذا أعتقه الزوج، أو كاتبه أو باعه قبل التسليم: صح؛ لأنه مثل من وجه، وعليه قيمته. إن حقها لا يعود إليه. ولهذا قلنا : إن كان القاضي قضى بقيمته على الزوج، ثم وهذه الجملة في نكاح الجامع الكبير مذكورة. ويتصل بهذه الجملة : أن مَن غصب طعاماً، فأطعمه المالك أن يُعلِمَه : لم يبرأ عند الشافعي رحمه الله ؛ لأنه ليس بأداء مأمور به؛ لأنه غُرور، إذ المرء لا يتحامى في العادات عن مال غيره في موضع الإباحة، والشرع لم يأمر بالغُرور، فبطل الأداء ؛ نفياً للغرور، فصار معنى الأداء لغواً؛ رداً للغرور. وقلنا نحن هذا أداء حقيقةً ؛ لأن عَيْنَ ماله وَصَلَ إلى يده، ولو كان قاصراً لتم بالهلاك، فكيف لا يتم وهو في الأصل كامل؟ وأما الخلل الذي ادعاه، فإنما وقع لجهله والجهل لا يُبطله، وكفى بالجهل عارا، فكيف يكون عذرا في تبديل إقامة الفرض اللازم. والعادة المخالفة للديانة الصحيحة على ما زعم: لغو؛ لأن وصل إلى يده. وأما القضاء بمثل معقول، فنوعان كامل، وقاصر. أما الكامل : فالمثل صورةً ومعنى، وهو الأصل في ضمان العدوان، وفي باب القروض ؛ تحقيقاً للجبر، حتى كان بمنزلة الأصل من كل وجه، فكان سابقا. وأما المثل القاصر : فالقيمة فيما له مثل إذا انقطع مثله، وفيما لا مثل له ؛ لأن حق المستحق في الصورة ،والمعنى إلا أن الحق في الصورة قد فات؛ للعجز عن القضاء به، فبقي في المعنى. ولهذا قال أبو حنيفة رضي الله عنه فيمن قطع يد رجلٍ عمداً، ثم قتله عمداً: أنه يقطعه الولي إن شاء، ثم يقتله ؛ لأنه مثل كامل، وأما القتل المنفرد : فمثل قاصر. وقالا : بل يقتله ولا يقطعه؛ لأن القتل بعد القطع تحقيق لموجب القطع ، فصار أمر الجناية يؤول إلى القتل. وقلنا هذا هكذا من طريق المعنى، فأما من طريق الصورة في باب : جزاء الفعل : فلا. ألا يُرى أن القتل قد يصلح ماحياً أثر القطع، كما يصلح محققاً؛ لأنه علة مبتدأة صالحة للحكم فوق الأول، فخيَّرناه بين الوجهين. ولهذا قلنا : لا يُضمَّن المثلي بالقيمة إذا انقطع المثلُ إلا يوم الخصومة عند أبي حنيفة رضي الله عنه؛ لأن المثل القاصر لا يصير مشروعاً مع احتمال الأصل، ولا ينقطع الاحتمال إلا بالقضاء.
And for this we said: She does not become free before possession until he hands it over to her, or it is decreed for her; because it is like (mithl) in some respect, so she does not own except by delivery. And for this we said: If the husband frees it, or makes a kitaba on it, or sells it before delivery: it is valid; because it is like in some respect, and he is liable for its value. Her right does not revert to him. And for this we said: If the judge had decreed its value against the husband, then this sentence is mentioned in the marriage (chapter) of al-Jami' al-Kabir. And connected to this sentence: That whoever usurps food, and the owner feeds him without informing him: he is not discharged according to al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him; because it is not a commanded performance; because it is deception (ghurur), since one does not ordinarily refrain from another's property in a situation of permissibility, and the Law did not command deception, so the performance becomes void; to negate deception, so the meaning of performance becomes null; in rejection of deception. And we (Hanafis) say: This is actually performance; because his actual property reached his hand, even if it were deficient it would be completed by destruction, so how is it not completed when originally it is complete? As for the defect he claimed, it only occurred due to his ignorance, and ignorance does not invalidate it, and sufficient is ignorance as a disgrace, so how can it be an excuse in substituting the performance of a necessary obligation? And the custom contrary to correct religion as he claimed: null; because it reached his hand. As for judging with a rational mithl, there are two types: complete and deficient. As for the complete: it is the mithl in form and meaning, and it is the original in compensation for aggression, and in the chapter of loans; to achieve restitution, so that it is like the original from every aspect, and it takes precedence. And as for the deficient mithl: it is the value for something that has a mithl when its mithl is unavailable, and for something that has no mithl; because the right of the claimant is in form and meaning, except that the right in form has been lost due to inability to fulfill it, so it remains in meaning. And for this Abu Hanifa, may Allah be pleased with him, said regarding one who intentionally cuts the hand of a man, then intentionally kills him: that the guardian may amputate him if he wishes, then kill him; because it is a complete mithl. And as for isolated killing: it is a deficient mithl. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: Rather, he kills him and does not amputate him; because killing after cutting affirms the requirement of cutting, so the matter of the injury leads to killing. And we said: This is so from the perspective of meaning; as for from the perspective of form in the chapter of penalty for the act: no. Do you not see that killing may serve to erase the effect of amputation, just as it serves to affirm it; because it is an independent cause suitable for a ruling above the first, so we gave him a choice between the two aspects. And for this we said: The owner of a mithli item is not liable for value when the mithl is unavailable except on the day of litigation according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah be pleased with him; because the deficient mithl does not become legislated while the original is possible, and possibility is not cut off except by judgment.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage is a multi-faceted discussion on the concept of al-mithl (likeness) in Hanafi law, specifically in compensation (daman) and punishments (qisas). The author begins by establishing rules regarding a wife's right to a slave given by her husband before delivery: she does not own it until possession. This is because the slave is considered 'mithl min wajh' (similar in some respect), so ownership is not complete without delivery. If the husband frees or sells before delivery, it is valid and he pays value. This leads to a connected case: ghasp (usurpation) of food. The Shafi'i position holds that if a usurper feeds the owner without informing him, it is not valid as repayment (ada') because it involves deception (ghurur). The Hanafi position, however, considers it valid ada' because the same property reaches its owner; ignorance does not invalidate it. The passage then explicitly defines two types of mithl in compensation: al-mithl al-kamil (complete likeness) which matches in form (surah) and meaning (ma'na), like returning the exact same item; and al-mithl al-qasir (deficient likeness) which is only value when the exact item is unavailable. An example from qisas: if someone cuts off a hand and then kills, Abu Hanifa allows both retaliation as a complete mithl (cutting then killing). The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that only killing is done because killing after cutting affirms the cutting's required punishment, leading to death. The author explains that both are valid from a meaning perspective, but from a form perspective the killing can either erase or affirm the cut. Finally, a rule: for mithli items (fungibles), if the mithl is unavailable, value is determined on the day of litigation according to Abu Hanifa, because the deficient mithl only becomes operative when the original mithl is impossible, which is only finalized by court judgment.

Key Terms
المثل الكامل (al-mithl al-kamil): The complete likeness that matches both form (surah) and meaning (ma'na), e.g., returning the exact usurped item.
المثل القاصر (al-mithl al-qasir): The deficient likeness, which is the value paid when the exact mithl is unavailable or the item has no mithl.
غرور (ghurur): Deception; in this context, feeding the owner without his knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the qisas example, what is Abu Hanifa’s ruling on a person who cuts a hand then kills the victim?
A) The guardian must only kill the offender, not amputate.
B) The guardian may amputate then kill, or only kill.
C) The guardian must only amputate, not kill.
D) The guardian may choose only one of the two punishments.

Key Takeaway
Compensation in Hanafi law centers on the concept of mithl: exact restitution (complete) is primary, and value (deficient) is a substitute that only becomes legally required when the original is deemed impossible by court judgment.

The Absolute Command and the Jumu'ah Dispute
Analyzing the absolute command's implications for Jumu'ah and Zuhr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the relationship between Jumu'ah and Zuhr and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the proof from qada and consensus.

Core Idea
The absolute command for Jumu'ah does not abrogate Zuhr; it is a unique obligation that, if missed, returns to the original.

This passage addresses a foundational dispute in usul al-fiqh: does an absolute command for a specific act (Jumu'ah) abrogate the general obligation (Zuhr)? The Hanafi school argues that it does not, using the evidence that Jumu'ah is never performed as qada, proving Zuhr remains the original. The Shafi'i position, also held by Zufar, views the command as indicating Jumu'ah's intrinsic goodness and sole validity for those addressed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue
Determine what exactly is disputed: whether the absolute command for Jumu'ah abrogates Zuhr or merely substitutes it.
The dispute centers on the interpretation of the command 'perform Jumu'ah after noon on Friday'.
2
State the Shafi'i/Zufar position and their dalil
They claim that the command shows Jumu'ah is the only valid prayer for residents at that time, making Zuhr invalid. For the excused, the command for Zuhr applies, making Zuhr good for them.
Their reasoning: the absolute command implies the best quality and sole legislative intent.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis argue that the command's modality is not abrogation. They point to the fact that when Jumu'ah is missed, Zuhr is performed as qada, and Jumu'ah is never performed as qada by consensus, proving Zuhr remains the original obligation.
This is a rational proof (talil) based on practice and consensus.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if Jumu'ah is missed, Hanafis say Zuhr is performed as qada; Shafi'is say Zuhr is not performed because Jumu'ah was the only obligation.
This affects the validity and requirement of Zuhr in such cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأمر المطلق في اقتضاء صفة الحسن يتناول الضرب الأول من القسم الأول ؛ لأن كمال الأمر يقتضي كمال صفة المأمور به.
وكذلك كونه عبادة: يقتضي هذا المعنى.
ويحتمل الضرب الثاني بدليل.
وعلى هذا قول الشافعي رحمه الله، وهو قول زفر لما تناول الأمر بعد الزوال يومَ الجمعة للجمعة : دلّ ذلك على صفة حسنه لعينه، وعلى أنه المشروع، دون غيره، حتى قالا : لا يصح أداء الظهر من المقيم ما لم تَفتِ الجمعة.
وقالا : لما لم يُخاطب المريض والعبد والمسافر بالجمعة، بل بالظهر : صار الظهرُ حَسَناً مشروعاً في حقهم، فإذا أدَّوْها: لم تنتقض بالجمعة من بعد.
وقلنا نحن لا خلاف في هذا الأصل، لكن الشأن في معرفة كيفية الأمر بالجمعة، وليس ذلك على نسخ الظهر كما قلتم.
ألا يُرى أنه بعد فوات الجمعة : يُقضى الظهر، والظهر لا يصلح أن يكون قضاء عن الجمعة ولا تُقضى الجمعة بالإجماع، فثبت أنه عَوْد إلى الأصل، وثبت أن قضية الأمر أداء الظهر بالجمعة، فصار ذلك مقرراً، لا فصح الأداء، وأمر بنقضه بالجمعة، كما أُمر بإسقاطه بالجمعة، ناسخاً، وإنما وضع عن المعذور أداء الظهر بالجمعة؛ رخصةً، فلم تبطل العزيمة.
وإنما قلنا إن الضرب الثالث من هذا القسم مختص بالأداء، دون القضاء، أما إذا فات الأداء في حال القدرة بتقصير المخاطب : فقد بقي تحت عُهدته، وجعل الشرط بمنزلة القائم حكماً؛ لتقصيره.
وأما إذا فات الأداء لا بتقصيره : فكذلك؛ لأن هذه القدرة كانت شرطاً لوجوب الأداء ؛ فضلاً من الله تعالى، فلم تشترط لبقاء الواجب.
ولهذا قلنا : لا يسقط بالموت في حقٌّ أحكام الآخرة.
ولهذا قلنا : إذا مَلَكَ الزاد والراحلة، فلم يحج حتى هلك المال: لم يبطل عنه الحج.
وكذلك صدقة الفطر ، لا تسقط بهلاك المال ؛ لما ذكرنا .
The absolute command in requiring the quality of goodness takes the first type of the first division; because the perfection of the command requires the perfection of the quality of the commanded act. And similarly its being an act of worship requires this meaning. And it admits the second type with a proof. Upon this is the statement of al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, and it is the statement of Zufar: when the command after noon on Friday applied to Friday prayer, that indicated the goodness of its essence, and that it is the legislated one, to the exclusion of others, until they both said: the performance of Zuhr by a resident is not valid unless Friday prayer is missed. And they said: since the sick, the slave, and the traveler are not addressed with Friday prayer but with Zuhr, Zuhr becomes good and legislated in their regard, so if they perform it, it is not invalidated by Friday prayer afterwards. And we said: there is no dispute in this principle, but the matter is in knowing the modality of the command regarding Friday prayer, and that is not about abrogating Zuhr as you claimed. Do you not see that after Friday prayer is missed, Zuhr is performed as qada, and Zuhr cannot be a substitute for Friday prayer, nor is Friday prayer performed as qada by consensus. So it is established that it is a return to the original, and it is established that the implication of the command is the performance of Zuhr (with Friday prayer taking precedence? unclear). So that became established, no invalidating of performance, and he ordered its annulment with Friday prayer, as he ordered its dropping with Friday prayer, as an abrogation. And indeed he placed for the excused person the performance of Zuhr (instead of Friday prayer) as a concession, so the determination is not invalidated by it. And we say: the third type of this division is specific to performance, not qada. As for if performance is missed while having ability due to the addressee's negligence, it remains under his responsibility, and the condition is made like existing provisionally due to his negligence. And as for if performance is missed not due to his negligence, likewise; because this ability was a condition for the obligation of performance, as a favor from Allah, so it is not conditioned for the persistence of the obligation. Therefore we say: it is not dropped by death regarding the rulings of the afterlife. Therefore we say: if one possesses provisions and mount, then does not perform Hajj until the wealth perishes, Hajj is not nullified from him. Likewise, zakah of breaking the fast (sadaqat al-fitr) is not dropped by the destruction of wealth, due to what we mentioned.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage addresses the nature of the absolute command and its relation to the quality of the commanded act, focusing on the dispute between the Hanafis and al-Shafi'i (and Zufar) regarding Friday prayer (Jumu'ah) and Zuhr. The author begins by stating that the absolute command demands the best quality of the commanded act, which is why it indicates the first type of obligation (the best form). However, it can also apply to a second type with evidence. The Shafi'i position, shared by Zufar, is that when the command for Jumu'ah after noon came, it showed that Jumu'ah is intrinsically good and the sole legislated prayer for those addressed, so Zuhr is invalid for a resident unless Jumu'ah is missed. For those excused (sick, slave, traveler) who are addressed with Zuhr, Zuhr becomes good and valid for them. The Hanafi response asserts agreement on the principle but differs on the modality of the command: the command for Jumu'ah does not abrogate Zuhr; rather, Zuhr remains the original obligation, and Jumu'ah is a unique obligation that, if missed, necessitates returning to Zuhr. This is proven by the fact that after missing Jumu'ah, Zuhr is performed as qada, and the fact that Jumu'ah itself is not performed as qada (consensus). Thus, Jumu'ah is like a substitution for Zuhr at its time, not an abrogation. The concession for the excused is a relaxation, not an invalidation of the original determination. The passage then discusses the third type of command (related to capability), stating that the first type of capability (qudrat al-tamkin) is a condition for the obligation of performance but not for the persistence of the obligation once it becomes due. Therefore, if the ability is lost after the obligation is established (e.g., wealth for Hajj or Zakat is lost), the obligation remains in the person's responsibility. This is supported by rulings: if one had the means for Hajj but lost them, Hajj is not nullified; likewise, sadaqat al-fitr is not dropped by the destruction of wealth after it becomes due. This section highlights the Hanafi distinction between conditions for the initial obligation and conditions for the continuing duty.

Key Terms
الأمر المطلق (al-amr al-mutlaq): An unqualified command that does not specify the exact manner or time, but generally implies the best quality of the commanded act.
صفة الحسن (sifat al-husn): The quality of goodness or correctness of an act in terms of fulfilling the command in the best possible manner.
قضاء (qada): Make-up or compensatory performance of an obligation after its prescribed time has passed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the status of Zuhr prayer for a resident when Jumu'ah is performed?
A) Zuhr becomes completely invalid for that day.
B) Zuhr remains the original obligation but is suspended during Jumu'ah time; if Jumu'ah is missed, Zuhr is performed as qada.
C) Zuhr is abrogated and never to be performed.
D) Jumu'ah is invalid if Zuhr is performed.

Key Takeaway
The absolute command for Jumu'ah does not abrogate Zuhr; Zuhr remains the original obligation, and Jumu'ah is a unique duty that, if missed, necessitates returning to Zuhr.

The Third Type of Command: Capability and Persistence of Obligation
Analyzing the third type of command and its implications for capability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that the condition for performance does not affect the persistence of an obligation once it becomes due, and apply it to cases of missed Hajj and zakat.

Core Idea
Once an obligation becomes due, the loss of ability does not erase it; it remains in the person's responsibility.

This section introduces the third type of command in Hanafi usul: obligations that depend on ability for performance but not for the obligation itself. It explains that if you had the means and failed to act, the duty remains, with examples from Hajj and sadaqat al-fitr. Understanding this principle is crucial for knowing when obligations become permanently binding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the third type of command
The third type (al-darb al-thālith) is specific to performance (adā'), not qada. It refers to obligations where ability (qudra) is a condition for the obligation to perform, but not for the obligation to persist.
This is a Hanafi classification.
2
Understand the condition of ability
Ability (qudrat al-tamkin) is a condition for the initial obligation to perform (wujūb al-adā'), but once the obligation is due, the loss of ability does not erase it.
This is a favor from Allah (faḍl min Allāh).
3
Apply the rule to cases of negligence
If performance is missed due to the addressee's negligence, the obligation remains (condition stands provisionally). If missed not due to negligence, it still remains because ability was only for initial obligation.
Example: if one had wealth for Hajj and lost it, Hajj is still obligatory (must be performed later if possible).
4
Derive the rulings for Hajj and zakat
The text gives two examples: if one possessed provisions for Hajj and then lost them, Hajj is not nullified. Similarly, sadaqat al-fitr is not dropped by the destruction of wealth after it becomes due.
These follow from the principle that the obligation persists.

Key Terms
الضرب الثالث (al-darb al-thālith): The third type (of command or obligation) that pertains solely to performance (adā'), not to make-up (qaḍā').
قدرة التمكين (qudrat al-tamkin): Ability that enables performance, viewed as a condition for the obligation to perform, not for the persistence of the obligation.
بقاء الواجب (baqā' al-wājib): The persistence of the obligation in the person's responsibility even after loss of the means to perform.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
12 min
Time as Measure and Cause: The Traveler's Fast in Ramadan
Intra-Hanafi dispute on traveler's Ramadan fast

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi concept of 'al-waqt al-muwaqqat' to identify when a time-bound obligation excludes other similar acts, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on the traveler's Ramadan fast.

Core Idea
In time-bound obligations where time is both measure and cause, the time excludes all other similar acts except the prescribed one.

This passage introduces a key distinction in Hanafi usul: between obligations where time is merely a condition (like prayer times) and those where time is both a measure (mi'yar) and cause (sabab) for the obligation, like Ramadan. From this distinction arises a dispute within the Hanafi school about whether a traveler can validly fast during Ramadan for non-obligatory purposes. The dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn hinges on whether the concession (rukhsa) to break the fast creates space for other legitimate acts within the same time.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish time as condition vs time as measure and cause.
Identify the two types of time-bound acts: the first where time is only a condition (e.g., prayer times), and the second where time is both a measure (mi'yar) and a cause (sabab) for the obligation, like the month of Ramadan. This distinction is foundational to understanding the dispute.
For the second type, the Law negates other acts in that time.
2
State the Sahibayn's position and their proof.
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad argue that since the time is exclusively for the obligatory Ramadan fast, no other fast is legislated for the traveler. The concession to break does not create a new legislated act. If the traveler fasts without intending Ramadan, his fast is void.
Their proof: the time is a measure and cause exclusively for Ramadan.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position and his proof.
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the obligation of Ramadan is still incumbent on the traveler; the concession is merely a license, not a negation. Thus the traveler can validly fast as Ramadan by 'azima (resolve). There are also narrations that voluntary fast may be valid if intended.
His proof: the obligation remains; the traveler is not required to break his fast.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).
If a traveler fasts with an unspecified intention, the Sahibayn rule it invalid, while Abu Hanifa counts it as Ramadan. This difference directly affects the validity of the fast.
The practical outcome depends on which view is followed.
5
Evaluate the role of 'azima (resolve) and rukhsa (concession).
Abu Hanifa emphasizes that choosing to fast is an act of 'azima, which is superior. The traveler's fast, if performed, fulfills his obligation. The Sahibayn give precedence to the exclusivity of the time over the traveler's choice.
This reflects different usul perspectives on the interaction between obligation and concession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشرط بالعوارض، ولا بتقصير العباد.
وأما النوع الثاني من المؤقتة فما جعل الوقت معياراً له، وسبباً لوجوبه، مثل شهر رمضان.
وإنما قلنا إنه معيار له ؛ لأنه قُدَّر وعُرف به ، وسبب له، وذلك شهودُ جزء من الشهر ؛ على ما نذكر في باب السبب إن شاء الله تعالى.
ومن حكمه: أن غيره صار منفياً؛ لأن الشرع لما أوجب شغل المعيار به، وهو واحد، فإذا ثبت له وصف: انتفى غيره، كالمكيل والموزون في معياره، فانتفى غيره ؛ لكونه غير مشروع.
قال أبو يوسف ومحمد رحمهما الله : ولما لم يبقَ غيره مشروعاً : لم يجز أداء الواجب فيه من المسافر ؛ لأن شَرْع الصوم فيه عام.
ألا يُرى أن صوم المسافر عن الفرض يجزئه، فثبت أنه مشروع في حقه، إلا أنه رُخص له أن يدعه بالفطر، وهذا لا يجعل غير الفرض مشروعاً، فانعدم فعله؛ لعدم ما نواه.
وكذلك على قولهما : إذا نوى النفل، أو أطلق النية.
وكذلك المريض في هذا كله.
وقال أبو حنيفة رحمه الله : الوجوب واقع على المسافر، ولهذا صح أداؤه بلا توقف إلا أنه رُخص له الترك ؛ قضاء لحقه، وتخفيفاً عليه، فلما ساغ له الترخص بما يرجع إلى مصالح بدنه : ففيما يرجع إلى مصالح دينه - قضاء ما عليه من الدين - أولى، وصار كونه ناسخاً لغيره متعلقاً بإعراضه عن جهة الرخصة، وتمسكه بالعزيمة وإذا لم يفعل بقي مشروعاً، فصح أداؤه.
ولأن الأداء غير مطلوب منه في سفره، فصار هذا الوقت في حق تسليم ما عليه بمنزلة شعبان، فقبل سائر الصيام.
والطريق الأول: يوجب أن لا يصح النفل بل يقع عن الفرض، والثاني: يوجب أن يصح، وفيه روايتان عنه.
وأما إذا أطلق النية : فالصحيح أن يقع عن رمضان؛ لأن الترخص والترك لا يتحقق بهذه العزيمة.
وأما المريض: فإن الصحيح عندنا فيه : أن يقع صومه بكل حال عن رمضان؛ لأن رخصته متعلقة بحقيقة العجز فيظهر بنفس الصوم فواتُ شرط الرخصة، فيلحق بالصحيح.
وأما المسافر: فيستوجب الرخصة بعجز مقدر بقيام سببه، وهو السفر، فلا يظهر بنفس الصوم فوات شرط الرخصة ، فلا يبطل الترخص. فيتعدى حينئذ بطريق التنبيه إلى حاجته الدينية.
قال زفر رحمه الله : ولما صار الوقت متعيّناً لهذا المشروع : صار ما يتصوّر من الإمساك في هذا الوقت مستحقاً على الفاعل، فيقع للمستحق بكل حال كصاحب النصاب إذا وهبه من الفقير بعد الحول، وكأجير الواحد يستحق منافعه.
قلنا : ليس التعيين باستحقاق لمنافع العبد ؛ لأن ذلك لا يصلح قُربة، وإنما القُربة فعل يفعله العبد عن اختيار بلا جبر، بل الشرع لم يشرع في هذا الوقت مما يتصور فيه الإمساك قُربةً إلا واحداً، فانعدم غير الفرض
The condition is due to accidents, not due to the shortcoming of the servants. As for the second type of time-bound (acts), it is that in which time is made a measure for it and a cause for its obligation, like the month of Ramadan. We only said it is a measure for it because it is determined and known by it, and a cause for it, and that is witnessing a part of the month, as we will mention in the chapter of cause, God willing. Among its rulings: that other than it is negated; because when the Law obligated the occupation of the measure with it, and it is one, when a description is established for it, other than it is negated, like measurable and weighable items in their measure, so other than it is negated because it is not legislated. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, may God have mercy on them, said: Since nothing other than it remained legislated, it is not permissible for the traveler to perform the obligation therein, because the legislation of fasting in it is general. Do you not see that the traveler's fasting for the obligation suffices him, so it is established that it is legislated with respect to him, except that he is given a concession to leave it by breaking the fast, and this does not make other than the obligation legislated, so his action is non‑existent due to the absence of what he intended. Likewise according to their statement: if he intended supererogatory or left the intention unspecified. And likewise the sick person in all this. Abu Hanifa, may God have mercy on him, said: The obligation is incumbent upon the traveler, and therefore its performance is valid without delay, except that he is given a concession to leave it, as a fulfillment of his right and a lightening for him. Since he is allowed to take a concession regarding what pertains to the interests of his body, then regarding what pertains to the interests of his religion—paying off what he owes of debt—is more appropriate, and his being abrogating other than it becomes dependent on his turning away from the aspect of concession and holding fast to the resolve, and if he does not do so, it remains legislated, so his performance is valid. And because performance is not required of him during his travel, so this time, with respect to fulfilling what is upon him, becomes like Sha'ban, accepting all fasts. The first way requires that supererogatory is not valid but falls as obligatory, and the second requires that it is valid, and there are two reports from him. As for when he leaves the intention unspecified, the correct [view] is that it falls as Ramadan, because concession and leaving are not realized by this resolve. As for the sick person, the correct according to us is that his fast falls in any case as Ramadan, because his concession is related to actual incapacity, so by the fast itself the loss of the condition of concession appears, and he is attached to the healthy person. As for the traveler, he becomes entitled to the concession due to an estimated incapacity by the existence of its cause, which is travel, so the loss of the condition of concession does not appear by the fast itself, so the concession is not invalidated. Then it extends by way of indication to his religious need. Zufar, may God have mercy on him, said: Since the time became specific to this legislated [act], what is conceivable of abstention in this time becomes due upon the doer, so it falls for the one entitled in any case, like the owner of the nisab if he gives it as a gift to a poor person after the year, and like a single employee whose benefits are due to him. We said: Specificity is not entitlement to the benefits of the servant, because that cannot be an act of worship; rather, an act of worship is an act done by the servant out of choice without compulsion. Rather, the Law did not legislate in this time, from what is conceivable of abstention, any act of worship except one, so other than the obligation is non‑existent.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage discusses a key dispute within the Hanafi school regarding the legal effect of time on obligations, specifically the fast of Ramadan. The text distinguishes two types of time-bound duties: those where time is only a condition for performance (like prayer times) and those where time is both a measure (mi'yar) and a cause (sabab) for the obligation, like Ramadan. In the latter, the time itself determines the obligation and excludes other fasts during that period. The core issue is whether a traveler (or sick person) can validly fast during Ramadan, and if so, what the fast counts for. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn) hold that since the time is exclusively for the obligatory Ramadan fast, no other fast is legislated during that time for the traveler. Thus, if a traveler fasts, it cannot count as anything other than the obligatory fast (if intended) or is void (if intended as supererogatory or unspecified). They argue that the concession (rukhsa) to break the fast does not make other fasts permissible; the time remains occupied by the obligation. Abu Hanifa holds that the obligation is established for the traveler, so the fast is valid as an obligation. The concession to break it is a concession, not a negation of the obligation. If the traveler chooses to fast (acting by ‘azima, resolve), his fast is valid as the obligatory Ramadan fast or, in one narration, as supererogatory if so intended. For the one who leaves the intention unspecified, the correct view is that it counts as Ramadan. For the sick person, the Hanafi position is that his fast always counts as Ramadan because his concession is based on actual incapacity, which disappears once he fasts. The passage also records Zufar's analogy that the time's specificity creates a claim on the person, like the zakah obligation. The author refutes this, stating that worship requires free choice, not compulsion. This dispute shows how different understandings of the nature of time and concession affect practical rulings on fasting during Ramadan.

Key Terms
الوقت المؤقت (al-waqt al-muwaqqat): A time-bound obligation where time is both a measure and a cause for the obligation, e.g., Ramadan.
المعيار (al-mi'yar): The measure that determines the quantity or scope of the obligation; here, time itself is the measure for the act of fasting.
السبب (as-sabab): The cause that triggers the obligation; here, the partial witnessing of the month (sighting of the crescent) is the cause for the duty of Ramadan fast.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), if a traveler fasts during Ramadan without specifying any intention, what is the ruling?
A) The fast counts as the obligatory Ramadan fast.
B) The fast counts as a voluntary fast.
C) The fast is invalid.
D) The fast is valid but makruh.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's concept of 'al-waqt al-muwaqqat' leads to an internal dispute on whether the traveler's fast in Ramadan can be other than the obligatory fast, with Abu Hanifa allowing flexibility through 'azima and the Sahibayn strictly enforcing time's exclusivity.
