The Mandatory Nature of Rukhsah: Qasr in Travel
Arguing that rukhsah (qasr) is mandatory ease, not optional choice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi argument that qasr is mandatory, identify the Shafi'i counter-argument, and apply the Hanafi principle of rukhsah to new cases.

Core Idea
Rukhsah mandates the easier option; the heavier obligation drops entirely because ease is determined by the Lawgiver.

This passage tackles a fundamental usul al-fiqh dispute: Is a concession (rukhsah) a permission to choose between two options, or does it replace the original ruling with a mandatory lighter one? The Hanafi school, through two rational proofs, argues that shortening the prayer (qasr) in travel is obligatory and the full prayer is invalid. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi reasoning and its response to Imam al-Shafi'i's literalist approach.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on qasr
The Hanafi school holds that the traveler must pray two rak'ahs for Dhuhr, Asr, and Isha. The four-rak'ah prayer is invalid. This is because the purpose of concession (rukhsah) is ease, and ease is determined by the Lawgiver, not by the servant's whim.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i adheres to the apparent meaning of the texts that allow shortening, interpreting them as granting the traveler a genuine choice between shortening and completing the prayer.
3
Follow the first Hanafi rational proof
If completing the prayer were allowed without extra reward, it would be pure burden, contradicting the purpose of ease. Since reward is for performing the obligation, and the obligation is determined by the Lawgiver, the full prayer drops entirely.
4
Follow the second Hanafi rational proof
Choice that does not benefit the servant is a divine prerogative; the servant only has the right to choose what is easier for himself. In qasr, the full prayer offers no benefit over the shortened one, so no real choice exists.
5
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical result: In the Hanafi school, a traveler who prays four rak'ahs must repeat the prayer (it is invalid). In the Shafi'i school, both two and four rak'ahs are valid, and the traveler may choose.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما المعنى فوجهان
أحدهما: أن الرخصة للتيسير، وقد تعيَّن اليُسر في القصر بيقين، فلا يبقى الإكمال إلا مؤنة محضةً، ليس فيها فضلُ ثواب؛ لأن الثواب في أداء ما عليه، فالقصر مع مؤنة السفر : مثلُ الإكمال، كقصر الجمعة مع إكمال الظهر، فوجب القول بالسقوط أصلاً.
والثاني : أن التخيير إذا لم يتضمن رفقاً بالعبد : كان ربوبيةً، وإنما للعباد اختيار الأرفق، فإذا لم يتضمن رفقاً بالعبد : كان ربوبية، ولا شركة له فيها.
ألا يُرى أن الشرع تولى وضعَ الشرائع جبراً، بخلاف التخيير في أنواع الكفارة ونحوها، لأنه يختار الأرفق عنده.
ولهذا لم تُجعل رخصة الصوم إسقاطاً؛ لأن النص جاء بالتأخير بقوله تعالى: ﴿فَعِدَّةٌ مِّنْ أَيَّامٍ أُخَرَ﴾ البقرة / ١٨٤، لا بالصدقة بالصوم.
وإنما إسقاط البعض في هذا نظيرُ التأخير، والحكم هو التأخير، واليُسر فيه متعارض؛ لأن الصوم في السفر يشق عليه من وجه؛ لسبب السفر، ويخِفٌ عليه من وجه بشركة المسلمين، وهي من أسباب اليسر، والتأخيرُ إلى أيام الإقامة يتعذر من وجه وهو الانفراد، ويخف من وجه، وهو الرفق بمرافق الإقامة.
والناس في الاختيار متفاوتون، فصار التخيير لطلب الرفق، فصار الاختيار ضرورياً، وللعبد اختيار ضروري، فأما مطلق الاختيار : فلا؛ لأنه إلهى، وصار الصوم أولى؛ لأنه أصل، وقد يشتمل على معنى الرخصة؛
لما قلنا وهو الذي وعدناه في أول هذا الفصل.
وإنما تمسك الشافعي رحمه الله في هذا الباب بظاهر العزيمة والرخصة، كما هو دأبه في دَرْك حدود الفقه، والله أعلم.
أربعاً،
هي
ولا يلزم على ما قلنا رجل أذن لعبده في الجمعة : أنه إن شاء صلى وهو الظهر، وإن شاء صلى ركعتين وهي الجمعة؛ لأن الجمعة الأصل عند الإذن، ولأنهما مختلفان، فاستقام طلب الرفق.
وكذلك مَن قال : إن دخلتُ الدارَ فعليَّ صيامُ سَنَةٍ، ففعل وهو معسر : كان له أن يصوم سنةً، أو يكفِّرَ بصيام ثلاثة أيام عند محمد رحمه الله.
وهو مروي في «النوادر» عن أبي حنيفة رضي الله عنه. أما في ظاهر الرواية : فيجب الوفاء به، لا محالة؛ لأن ذلك مختلف في المعنى، أحدهما: قُربةٌ مقصودة، والثاني: كفارة.
وفي مسألتنا : هما سواء، فصار كالمدبر إذا جنى: لزم مولاه الأقل من الأرش، ولا يلزم أن موسى عليه السلام كان مخيَّراً بين أن يرعى غَنَمَ شعيب عليه السلام ثماني حِجَج، أو عشراً، فيما ضمن من المهر؛ لأن الثمانية كانت مهراً لازماً، والفضل كان براً منه، والله أعلم.
ويتصل بهذه الجملة معرفة حكم الأمر والنهي في ضد ما نُسبا إليه، وهذا تابع غير مقصود في جنس الأحكام؛ فأخرناه.
As for the meaning (of the concession), there are two aspects. One: The concession is for ease, and ease in shortening (the prayer) is determined with certainty, so completing it (the full prayer) remains only pure burden, with no extra reward, because reward is for performing what is obligatory. So shortening (qasr) with the hardship of travel is equivalent to completing it, like shortening Friday prayer (to two rak'ahs) compared with completing Dhuhr (four rak'ahs). Therefore, it is necessary to say that it (the full prayer) drops entirely. Second: If choice does not involve benefitting the servant, it is a divine prerogative; the servants only have the choice of the more beneficial. So if it does not involve benefitting the servant, it is a divine prerogative, and they have no share in it. Do you not see that the Lawgiver imposed the laws by compulsion, unlike the choice in types of expiation and the like, because one chooses the more beneficial in his view. For this reason, the concession for fasting was not made a cancellation (of the obligation), because the text came with postponement by His statement: {then a number of other days} (Quran 2:184), not with giving charity instead of fasting. Rather, the cancellation of part in this is similar to postponement, and the ruling is postponement, and the ease in it is conflicting, because fasting while traveling is burdensome from one aspect due to the journey, but becomes light from another aspect by sharing with the Muslims, which is a cause of ease. Postponement to days of residence is problematic from one aspect—being alone—and easy from another aspect—the comfort of residence. People vary in their ability to choose, so choice became for seeking comfort, and thus choice became necessary. The servant has a necessary choice, but absolute choice is not allowed because it is divine. Fasting became better because it is the original (obligation) and sometimes includes the meaning of concession. (This is) as we said, which we promised at the beginning of this chapter. Al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, only adhered in this chapter to the apparent meaning of determination (azimah) and concession, as is his habit in grasping the limits of jurisprudence. And Allah knows best. Four (points). The following does not contradict what we said: a man who permitted his slave for Friday prayer—if he wishes, he prays Dhuhr (four rak'ahs), and if he wishes, he prays two rak'ahs, which is Friday—because Friday is the original upon permission, and because the two prayers are different, so seeking ease is appropriate. Similarly, one who says, 'If I enter the house, I must fast a year,' and does so while he is poor: he may fast a year or expiate by fasting three days according to Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him. And it is narrated in al-Nawadir from Abu Hanifa, may Allah be pleased with him. As for Zahir al-Riwayah, fulfillment (of the vow) is necessary without fail, because those (two options) differ in meaning: one is a deliberate act of worship, the other is expiation. In our case (qasr vs. full prayer), they are equal. So it becomes like a mudabbar (a slave whose freedom is deferred after master's death) if he commits a crime: the master is liable for the lesser of the two values (the slave's value or the injury). And it does not follow that Moses, peace be upon him, was given a choice between tending the sheep of Shu'ayb, peace be upon him, for eight years or ten years, as part of the promised dowry, because the eight were an obligatory dowry, and the extra was a voluntary act from him. And Allah knows best. Connected to this discussion is the knowledge of the ruling of command and prohibition regarding their opposites—this is a subordinate matter not intended in the category of rulings, so we have postponed it.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the nature of concession (rukhsah), specifically regarding shortening the prayer (qasr) during travel. The author gives two rational arguments for why the concession must be interpreted as a mandatory lighter obligation rather than a choice between equal options. First, since the lawgiver intends ease, and shortening is unequivocally easier, completing the prayer would be a pure burden with no extra reward, so it cannot be permitted. Second, if choice does not benefit the servant, it is a divine prerogative; the servant can only choose what is easier. The author compares this to the concession for fasting, where the Quran commands postponement, not an alternative act. The ease in fasting is conflicting because of shared worship and individual burden, so choice is necessary but not absolute. The Hanafi position is that the servant has a 'necessary choice' (ikhtiyar daruri) but not absolute choice, which is divine. The author then refutes al-Shafi'i's view, which adheres to the literal meanings of 'azimah (determination) and rukhsah (concession) as both valid options. To illustrate, he gives two exceptions: a master permitting his slave for Friday prayer does not give a choice between Dhuhr and Friday because Friday is the original intention, and they differ in nature. In contrast, a vow to fast a year: according to Muhammad and a narration in al-Nawadir, the poor person may choose to fast a year or expiate with three days of fasting, but in Zahir al-Riwayah the vow is binding. The difference is that in our case (qasr) the two prayers are equal in essence (two rak'ahs vs. four), whereas in the vow case fasting and expiation differ in meaning. Finally, the author notes that the ruling of command and prohibition regarding their opposites will be discussed later as a subordinate topic.

Key Terms
رخصة (rukhsah): A concession that lightens an obligation due to a valid excuse, interpreted by the Hanafis as a mandatory lighter obligation (not a choice).
تخيير (takhyir): Choice between two alternatives; when applied to concessions, the Hanafis argue it is not absolute choice but a 'necessary choice' (ikhtiyar daruri) because only the easier option fulfills the purpose of the Lawgiver.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The transmitted opinions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad in the six major works (al-Umm, etc.), considered the authoritative position of the school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how should a traveler pray Dhuhr during a journey?
A) He may choose between praying two rak'ahs or four.
B) He must pray two rak'ahs; the four-rak'ah prayer is invalid.
C) He must pray four rak'ahs unless he chooses to shorten.
D) He prays two rak'ahs if he wants, but four is better.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, rukhsah (concession) is not a mere permission but a mandatory lighter obligation, because the Lawgiver's purpose of ease overrides the literal option of choice.

Does a Command Prohibit Its Opposite? — The Hanafi Theory of Iqtida
Debate whether command implies prohibition of its opposite

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three positions on whether a command implies prohibition of its opposite and apply the Hanafi concept of iqtida to determine the ruling of an opposite act that does not nullify the command.

Core Idea
A command does not primarily prohibit its opposite; the prohibition is a necessary but unintended consequence (iqtida), making non-nullifying opposites merely disliked.

This passage from Usul al-Bazdawi addresses a key dispute in usul al-fiqh: does a command automatically make its opposite prohibited? Al-Jassas argued yes, because existence cannot coexist with any opposite. The third group argued for a minimal implication. The Hanafi position distinguishes between the intended meaning of the command and its necessary consequences (iqtida). Understanding this distinction is vital for deriving rulings in cases like standing and sitting in prayer, and the dress of a muhrim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
Step through al-Jassas, the third group, and the author's (Bazdawi's) chosen view. Note how each understands the relationship between command and opposite.
Al-Jassas: command prohibits all opposites necessarily. Third group: minimal implication needed. Author: iqtida – necessary but not intended.
2
Trace the rational argument
Understand al-Jassas' rational argument: a command requires existence of the commanded act, which cannot coexist with any opposite, so all opposites are prohibited by necessity.
This is a dalil aqli (rational proof).
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The author refutes al-Jassas' examples (e.g., concealment of menstruation is a cancellation, not a prohibition) and introduces iqtida: a necessary consequence that is not the intended ruling.
The verse is interpreted as naskh (cancellation) rather than nahy.
4
Apply the principle
See the practical benefit (fa'idah): if the opposite act does not nullify the command, it is merely makruh, not haram. Example: sitting during prayer (when standing is commanded) is disliked but does not invalidate the prayer if one then stands.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical result of the dispute).
5
Distinguish single vs. multiple opposites
For a prohibition, if there is only one opposite, it is automatically implied. If multiple opposites exist, not all are required to be performed; only the opposite that directly nullifies the prohibition is relevant.
Example: muhrim is prohibited from sewn garments, but not commanded to wear a specific unsewn garment.

Source Text

واحتج الجصاص رحمه الله : بأن الأمر بالشيء وضع لوجوده، ولا وجود له مع الاشتغال بشيء من أضداده، فصار ذلك من ضرورات حكمه. وأما النهي : فإنه للتحريم. ومن ضرورته : فعل ضده إذا كان له ضد واحد كالحركة والسكون فأما إذا تعدد الضد : فليس من ضرورة الكف عنه : إتيان كل أضداده، ألا يرى أن المأمور بالقيام إذا قعد، أو نام، أو اضطجع : فقد فوت المأمور والمنهي عن القيام : لا يُفوِّتُ حكم النهي، بأن يقعد، أو ينام، أو يضطجع. قال: وأجمع الفقهاء رحمهم الله أن المرأة منهية عن كتمان الحيض بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا يَحِلُّ لَهُنَّ أَن يَكْتُمْنَ مَا خَلَقَ اللَّهُ فِي أَرْحَامِهِنَّ ﴾ البقرة / ۲۲۸ ، ثم كان ذلك أمراً بالإظهار ؛ لأن الكتمان ضده واحد، وهو الإظهار. واتفقوا أن المُحرِمَ منهي عن لبس المخيط، ولم يكن مأموراً بلبس شيء متعين من غير المخيط. واحتج الفريق الثالث : بأن الأمر على ما قال الجصاص رحمه الله ، إلا أنَّا أثبتنا بكل واحد من القسمين أدنى ما يثبت به؛ لأن الثابت لغيره ضرورةً : لا يساوي المقصود بنفسه. - وأما الذي اخترناه فبناءً على هذا وهو أن هذا لما كان أمراً ضرورياً سميناه اقتضاء، ومعنى الاقتضاء ها هنا: أنه ضروري غير مقصود، فصار شبيهاً بما ذكرنا من مقتضيات أحكام الشرع. وأما قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَلَا يَحِلُّ هُنَّ أَن يَكْتُمْنَ) البقرة/ ۲۲۸ : فليس بنهي، بل نسخ له أصلاً، مثل قوله تعالى: (لَا يَحِلُّ لَكَ النِّسَاءُ مِنْ بَعْدُ الأحزاب / ٥٢ ، فلا يصير الأمر ثابتاً بالنهي، بل لأن الكتمان لم يبق مشروعاً؛ لما تعلَّق بإظهاره من أحكام الشرع، فصار بهذه الواسطة أمراً. وهذا مثل قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «لانكاح إلا بشهود»). وفائدة هذا الأصل: أن التحريم إذا لم يكن مقصوداً بالأمر : لم يُعتبر إلا من حيث يُفوِّت الأمر، فإذا لم يُفوِّتُه : كان مكروهاً، كالأمر بالقيام: ليس بنهي عن القعود قصداً، حتى إذا قعد، ثم قام: لم تفسد صلاته بنفس القعود، ولكنه يكره. ولهذا قلنا: إن المُحرِم لما نهي عن لبس المخيط : كان من السنة لُبس الإزار والرداء . ولهذا قلنا: إن العدة لما كان معناها النهي عن الخروج والتزوج : يكن الأمر بالكف مقصوداً، حتى انقضت الأعداد منها بزمان واحد.
Al-Jassas (may Allah have mercy on him) argued: The command for a thing is placed for its existence, and its existence does not occur while engaging in any of its opposites; thus that is among the necessities of its ruling. As for prohibition, it is for prohibition (tahrim). And from its necessity is doing its opposite if it has a single opposite, like movement and stillness. But if the opposite is multiple, then it is not necessary from refraining from it to bring about all its opposites. Do you not see that the one commanded to stand, if he sits, sleeps, or lies down, he has nullified the command; and the one prohibited from standing does not nullify the ruling of the prohibition by sitting, sleeping, or lying down. He said: The jurists (may Allah have mercy on them) have agreed that the woman is prohibited from concealing menstruation by the statement of Allah Most High: {And it is not lawful for them to conceal what Allah has created in their wombs} (al-Baqarah 2:228), then that was a command to disclose; because concealment has one opposite, which is disclosure. And they agreed that the muhrim is prohibited from wearing sewn clothes, and he was not commanded to wear a specific thing from unsewn clothes. The third group argued: The command is as al-Jassas stated, except that we have established for each of the two categories the least that proves it; because that which is established for another by necessity is not equal to that which is intended by itself. As for what we have chosen, it is based on this: that since this was a necessary matter, we called it 'iqtida' (necessity), and the meaning of iqtida here is that it is necessary, not intended. Thus it becomes similar to what we mentioned of the necessary implications of the rulings of the Shari'ah. As for the statement of Allah Most High: {And it is not lawful for them to conceal} (al-Baqarah 2:228), it is not a prohibition, but rather a cancellation (naskh) of it entirely, like His statement: {It is not lawful for you (to take) women from after} (al-Ahzab 33:52). Thus the command is not established by the prohibition, but rather because concealment is no longer legislated due to the rulings of the Shari'ah attached to its disclosure, so it becomes a command through this intermediary. And this is like his statement, peace be upon him: ‘No marriage except with witnesses.’ And the benefit of this principle is that when the prohibition is not intended by the command, it is only considered from where it nullifies the command; if it does not nullify it, it is disliked (makruh). Like the command to stand: it is not intentionally a prohibition of sitting, so if he sits then stands, his prayer is not invalidated by the sitting itself, but it is disliked. And for this we said: Since the muhrim is prohibited from wearing sewn clothes, it is from the Sunnah to wear the izaar and rida. And for this we said: Since the meaning of iddah is the prohibition of exiting and marrying, the command to refrain is not intended, so that the iddah periods are completed in one time.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Bazdawi addresses a fundamental question in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: Does a command (amr) necessarily imply the prohibition (nahy) of its opposite? The author presents three positions, critiques them, and establishes his own view that the prohibition of the opposite is a necessary consequence (iqtida) of the command, but it is not the intended meaning; it is a necessary implication rather than a primary objective.

Al-Jassas argues that a command requires the existence of the commanded act, which cannot coexist with any of its opposites; thus the prohibition of all opposites is a necessary consequence. For prohibition, the implication is the doing of a single opposite if only one exists; if multiple, not all are required. He supports this with the consensus that women are prohibited from concealing menstruation (which becomes a command to disclose, as concealment has one opposite), and that a muhrim is prohibited from sewn clothes but not commanded to wear a specific unsewn garment.

The third group agrees with al-Jassas on the command but adds that for each category, only the minimal requirement is established; the necessary implication is not equal to the intended ruling.

The author (Bazdawi) chooses to call the necessary implication 'iqtida' — something necessary but not the intended object of the command. He refutes the example of concealment of menstruation, arguing that the verse is not a prohibition but a cancellation (naskh) of concealment itself; the command to disclose arises indirectly. Similarly, the hadith 'No marriage except with witnesses' functions the same way.

The practical benefit (fa'idah) of this principle: When a prohibition is not the intended meaning of a command, it is only relevant if it nullifies the command. If it does not nullify, it is merely disliked (makruh). Examples: sitting during prayer without invalidating it is disliked; for the muhrim, it is sunnah to wear specific unsewn garments; for a woman in iddah, the prohibition of exiting and marriage is not the intended command, so the iddah can be completed in one period.

Key Terms
الضد (al-didd): An opposite act that prevents the existence of the commanded or prohibited act, e.g., sitting is the opposite of standing.
الاقتضاء (al-iqtida): A necessary consequence of a ruling that is not intended by the ruling itself, like the prohibition of an opposite arising from a command.
الأمر (al-amr): A demand to perform an act from a higher authority; it implies the existence of the commanded act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author (Bazdawi), what is the status of an act that is the opposite of a commanded act but does not nullify the command?
A) It is haram (prohibited) because it contradicts the command.
B) It is wajib (obligatory) to avoid it.
C) It is makruh (disliked) but not haram.
D) It is permissible (mubah) without any dislike.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi concept of iqtida teaches that necessary implications of a ruling are not the intended object of that ruling, affecting the degree of prohibition (makruh vs haram).

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
10 min
When Does a Khabar al-Wahid Conflict with Qiyas?
Debating the authority of a hadith conflicting with qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a khabar al-wahid which agrees with qiyas is a valid proof (hujja), and distinguish this from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
A khabar al-wahid is not automatically overridden by qiyas; it is rejected only if it clearly contradicts established analogy.

This lesson examines a foundational usul dispute: what happens when a solitary hadith (khabar al-wahid) appears to conflict with qiyas? The Hanafi school argues that such a hadith remains a valid proof if it does not actually contradict their own qiyas. We will study the famous case of Buraw' bint Washiq, where the Prophet (ﷺ) ruled that a woman whose husband died without fixing a dower is entitled to the dower of her peers. This hadith was accepted by Ibn Mas'ud but rejected by Ali and later by Imam al-Shafi'i. Through this example, you will learn how the Hanafis navigate between textual evidence and analogical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue and the two positions
Clarify that the dispute is about the authority of a khabar al-wahid that appears to contradict qiyas. The Hanafis hold it as hujja if it agrees with their qiyas; the Shafi'is reject it because it contradicts their qiyas.
The key is that each school's qiyas differs, so the same hadith may be accepted by one and rejected by the other.
2
Locate the primary proof (the hadith) and evaluate its transmission
Examine the hadith of Ma'qil ibn Sinan: the Prophet's ruling for Buraw' bint Washiq. Note that it is narrated by reliable narrators (thiqat) such as Ibn Mas'ud, Alqama, Masruq, etc. The Hanafis stress that multiple trustworthy narrators support it.
The text mentions that tribal members of Ashja' also testified to the hadith, strengthening its authority.
3
Understand the role of qiyas in each school's methodology
The Hanafis have a specific qiyas that would also give the woman a dower, so the hadith aligns with their qiyas. The Shafi'is have a different qiyas that would give no dower, so the hadith conflicts with their qiyas.
This shows why the same hadith can be hujja for one school and not for another.
4
Examine the Hanafi claim that the hadith agrees with their qiyas
The text states: 'وعندنا هو حجة؛ لأنه وافق القياس عندنا' (With us it is a proof because it agrees with analogy according to us). The Hanafis assert that their qiyas supports the ruling of mahr al-mithl.
The Hanafi response to the Shafi'i objection is that the hadith does not actually oppose their qiyas.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) and why it matters
The ruling for a woman whose husband dies without fixing a dower: Hanafis give her mahr al-mithl (dower of peers); Shafi'is give her inheritance and no dower. This difference has real financial implications.
Understanding this dispute helps clarify the broader usul principle of prioritizing textual evidence over reasoning when they align.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
موضع الحاجة إلى البيان: بيان ، ولا يُتّهم السلف بالتقصير.
٤ - وإن اختلف فيه مع نقل الثقات عنه : فكذلك عندنا، مثل حديث معقل بن سنان أبي محمد الأشجعي في حديث بروع بنت واشق الأشجعية أنه مات عنها زوجها هلالُ بن أبي مُرَّة، ولم يكن فَرَضَ لها مهراً، ولا دخل بها، فقضى لها رسولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بمهر مثل نسائها.
فَعَمِل بحديثه عبد الله بن مسعود رضي الله عنه، ورده علي رضي الله عنه لما خالف رأيه، وقال: «ما نصنعُ بقول أعرابي بوال على عقبيه»
ولم يعمل الشافعي رحمه الله بهذا القسم ؛ لأنه خالف القياس عنده.
وعندنا هو حجة؛ لأنه وافق القياس عندنا، وإنما يُترك إذا خالف القياس. وقد روى عنه الثقاتُ، مثل عبد الله بن مسعود، وعلقمة، ومسروق، ونافع بن جبير والحسن البصري رضي الله عنهم، فثبتت بروايتهم عدالته، أنه مع من قَرْن العدول ، فلذلك صار حجةً، وساعده عليه أناس من أشجع منهم أبو الجراح، وغيره.
(١) قوله : عَمِل به ابن مسعود : يفسره ما تقدم، وقد أخرجه ابن أبي شيبة، وفيه: فما رأيت ابن مسعود فرح بشيء ما فرح يومئذ به.
(٢) قوله : وردَّه علي لما خالف رأيه، وقال ما نصنع بقول أعرابي بوال على عقبيه : لم أقف عليه بهذا اللفظ، وإنما أخرج عبد الرزاق عن الحكم بن عتيبة: «أن علياً كان يجعل لها الميراث، وعليها العدة، ولا يجعل لها صداقاً». قال الحكم وأخبر بقول ابن مسعود، فقال: لا نُصدَّقُ الأعراب على رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم. وأخرجه ابن أبي شيبة ثنا ابن عيينة عن عمرو وعطاء بن السائب عن عبد خيرٍ يرى أنه عن علي قال لها الميراث، ولا صداق لها. ثنا أبو معاوية عن الشيباني عن عمرو بن مرة عمن أخبره عن علي قال لها الميراث، ولا صداق لها.
(١) قوله : وقد روى عنه الثقات مثل عبد الله بن مسعود وعلقمة ومسروق ونافع بن جبير والحسن، أما رواية ابن مسعود : فلم أقف عليها التحديث عنه ، بصريح وإنما قَبِل منه، وصدقه، وفرح بما أخبره به ، وأما رواية علقمة عنه: فعند الأربعة، ورواية مسروق عنه : عند أبي داود والنسائي وابن ماجه ورواية نافع بن جبير عنه : عند أحمد في المسند، ورواية الحسن البصري عنه : عند النسائي، وكذا الأسود بن يزيد، والله أعلم.
(٢) قوله : وساعده عليه ناس من أشجع منهم أبو الجراح، وغيره: أما رواية أبي الجراح فأخرجها أبو داود فقال الجراح، ولفظه: «فقام ناس من أشجع فيهم الجراح وأبو سنان فقالوا: يابن مسعود نحن نشهد أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قضاها فينا في بروع بنت واشق وإن زوجها هلال بن مرة الأشجعي كما قضيت». الحديث.
وقال أبو موسى في معرفة الصحابة»: أبو الجراح. وعند النسائي: «أُتي عبد الله بن مسعود في امرأة توفي عنها زوجها قبل أن يُفرض لها الحديث، وفيه : فقام سلمة وفلان وفلان فشهدوا أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قضى في بروع بنت واشق. الحديث.
وعنده في رواية : فقام رجل من أشجع - قال منصور: أراه سلمة بن يزيد فقال : مثل هذا قضى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في بروع». الحديث.
وعند أحمد: «فقام رجل من أشجع فقال أشهد على النبي صلى الله عليه
The place of need for clarification: a clarification, and the predecessors are not accused of negligence.
4 - And if there is disagreement about it while reliable narrators have transmitted it: then it is the same with us, like the hadith of Ma'qil ibn Sinan Abu Muhammad al-Ashja'i concerning the hadith of Buraw' bint Washiq al-Ashja'iyya that her husband Hilal ibn Abi Murra died, and he had not fixed a dower for her nor consummated the marriage. So the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) judged for her a dower like that of her peers.
Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (may God be pleased with him) acted upon his hadith, but Ali (may God be pleased with him) rejected it because it opposed his opinion, saying: “What shall we do with the word of a Bedouin who urinates on his heels?”
Al-Shafi'i (may God have mercy on him) did not act upon this category because it opposed analogy according to him.
But with us it is a proof because it agrees with analogy according to us; it is only abandoned if it opposes analogy. And reliable narrators have transmitted it from him, such as Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, Alqama, Masruq, Nafi' ibn Jubayr, and al-Hasan al-Basri (may God be pleased with them). So his trustworthiness is established through their narration, that he is among the group of upright ones; therefore it became a proof. And some people from Ashja' supported him, among them Abu al-Jarrah and others.
(1) His statement: Ibn Mas'ud acted upon it: This is explained by what preceded, and Ibn Abi Shayba narrated it, and in it: I have not seen Ibn Mas'ud rejoice at anything as he rejoiced that day.
(2) His statement: Ali rejected it because it opposed his opinion, saying: What shall we do with the word of a Bedouin who urinates on his heels? I have not found it with this wording, but Abd al-Razzaq narrated from al-Hakam ibn Utayba: “Ali gave her inheritance, imposed the waiting period on her, and gave her no dower.” Al-Hakam said: He was informed of Ibn Mas'ud's statement, so he said: We do not take the word of Bedouins over the Messenger of God (peace be upon him). Ibn Abi Shayba narrated: Ibn Uyayna from Amr and Ata ibn al-Sa'ib from Abd Khayr who thought it was from Ali: He said: She has inheritance, and no dower for her. Also from Abu Muawiya from al-Shaybani from Amr ibn Murra from someone who told him from Ali: He said: She has inheritance, and no dower for her.
(1) His statement: And reliable narrators have transmitted it from him such as Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, Alqama, Masruq, Nafi' ibn Jubayr, and al-Hasan al-Basri: As for the narration of Ibn Mas'ud: I have not found it explicitly as a hadith from him, but he accepted it, believed him, and rejoiced at what he told him. As for the narration of Alqama from him: it is in the four [Sunan]. The narration of Masruq from him: in Abu Dawud, al-Nasa'i, and Ibn Majah. The narration of Nafi' ibn Jubayr from him: in Ahmad's Musnad. The narration of al-Hasan al-Basri from him: in al-Nasa'i, and also al-Aswad ibn Yazid. And God knows best.
(2) His statement: And some people of Ashja' supported him, among them Abu al-Jarrah and others: As for the narration of Abu al-Jarrah, Abu Dawud narrated it saying al-Jarrah, and its wording: “Some people of Ashja' stood up, among them al-Jarrah and Abu Sinan, and said: O Ibn Mas'ud, we bear witness that the Prophet (peace be upon him) judged concerning Buraw' bint Washiq, and her husband Hilal ibn Murra al-Ashja'i, just as you have judged.” The hadith.
And Abu Musa said in 'Ma'rifat al-Sahaba': Abu al-Jarrah. And in al-Nasa'i: “Abdullah ibn Mas'ud was consulted about a woman whose husband died before fixing a dower for her... the hadith, and in it: Salama and so-and-so and so-and-so stood up and testified that the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) gave a judgment concerning Buraw' bint Washiq.” The hadith.
And in his narration: “A man of Ashja' stood up - Mansur said: I think he was Salama ibn Yazid - and said: ‘The Messenger of God (peace be upon him) gave such a judgment concerning Buraw'.’” The hadith.
And in Ahmad: “A man of Ashja' stood up and said: ‘I bear witness that the Prophet (peace be upon him)…”
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute concerning the status of a khabar al-wahid (solitary report) that appears to conflict with qiyas (analogy). The specific example is the hadith of Ma'qil ibn Sinan about Buraw' bint Washiq, where the Prophet (ﷺ) ruled that a woman whose husband died without fixing a dower is entitled to the dower of her peers. The Hanafi position is that this hadith is a valid proof (hujja) because, according to their own qiyas, it does not actually contradict analogy; rather, it agrees with it. The Shafi'i school, however, rejects this category of hadith because, according to their qiyas, it does contradict analogy. The text notes that the hadith was accepted and acted upon by Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, but rejected by Ali, who famously dismissed it as the word of a Bedouin. The Hanafis argue that the hadith is transmitted by reliable narrators (thiqat) such as Ibn Mas'ud, Alqama, Masruq, Nafi' ibn Jubayr, and Hasan al-Basri, and therefore its authority is established. Additionally, other members of the Ashja' tribe, including Abu al-Jarrah, supported its authenticity. The footnotes provide additional chain details and variations. The key takeaway is that the Hanafi school does not automatically reject a khabar al-wahid that seems contrary to qiyas; rather, they first examine whether it truly contradicts their own qiyas. If it does not, it remains a valid proof.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A report transmitted by one or a few narrators, not reaching tawatur.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning derived from primary sources to extend rulings to new cases.
حجة (hujja): A valid proof that establishes a Shari'a ruling and must be followed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis accept the hadith of Ma'qil ibn Sinan about Buraw' bint Washiq as a proof?
A) Because it is narrated by many chains reaching tawatur
B) Because it agrees with Hanafi qiyas and is transmitted by reliable narrators
C) Because Imam Shafi'i accepted it
D) Because it was narrated by Abdullah ibn Mas'ud alone

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts a khabar al-wahid as a proof unless it clearly contradicts established qiyas; the hadith of Buraw' bint Washiq is accepted because it agrees with Hanafi qiyas.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

The Dispute Over Fatimah bint Qays' Hadith: Rejecting a Khabar al-Wahid
Narrations and opinions disputing the hadith of Fatimah bint Qays

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the factors that can lead to the rejection of a khabar al-wahid even when its chain is technically sound, using the dispute over Fatimah bint Qays' narration as a case study.

Core Idea
A sound khabar al-wahid may be rejected if the narrator is questioned or the ruling contradicts established practice.

This passage presents a classic usul al-fiqh dispute: the hadith of Fatimah bint Qays, reported by a single narrator, states that a thrice-divorced woman is entitled to neither housing nor maintenance unless pregnant. Yet many Companions and later scholars rejected this report. Why? The Hanafi school uses this case to illustrate that acceptance of a khabar al-wahid requires not only a sound chain but also the narrator's reliability and the absence of conflict with stronger evidence or general practice. By examining the objections and responses, you will learn the nuanced criteria for accepting solitary reports.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith and its ruling
Locate the narration attributed to Fatimah bint Qays in the passage. What ruling does the Prophet (peace be upon him) give her? The text states: 'No maintenance for you nor housing unless you are pregnant.' This is the core report.
The hadith is a khabar al-wahid (solitary report).
2
Note the objections from Companions and scholars
Examine the objections raised by Aisha, Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib, Marwan, and others. What reasons do they give? Aisha says Fatimah was in a 'wild house' and feared for her safety, so the concession was specific. Ibn al-Musayyib says Fatimah 'misled people' and 'extended her tongue'. Marwan says he never heard this report except from a woman.
These objections attack either the specific application or the narrator's general reliability.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
How does the Hanafi school reconcile the hadith with the objections? The response is that the ruling of the hadith is specific to Fatimah's case due to her quarrelsome nature or safety concerns, and the general principle (from Quran 65:6) that a divorced woman is entitled to housing remains. The Hanafis accept the hadith but limit its application.
This shows that khabar al-wahid can be interpreted narrowly.
4
Derive the usul principle
From this dispute, extract the principle about accepting khabar al-wahid. Even a technically sound report may be rejected if contradicted by general practice (amal, or 'what the people were upon'), if the narrator is considered unreliable (even by virtue of memory or character), or if the report describes an exceptional situation (khususiyyah). In Hanafi usul, these factors can prevent a khabar al-wahid from establishing a general rule.
This principle is key to evaluating isolated reports.

And in a narration: 'Aisha greatly disapproved of that and said: Fatimah was in a wild house, and it was feared for her side, so for that reason the Messenger of Allah gave her a concession.' I said: Did the Messenger of Allah not order Fatimah bint Qays to observe iddah in the house of Ibn Umm Maktum? And from Abu Salamah ibn Abd al-Rahman: Fatimah told him that the Messenger of Allah said to her: Observe iddah in the house of Ibn Umm Maktum; so the people disapproved of her mentioning her departure before she became permissible. Both reported by al-Tahawi and others.
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute in Hanafi usul: the acceptance of khabar al-wahid. The hadith of Fatimah bint Qays, reported by her alone, indicates that a thrice-divorced woman has no housing or maintenance unless pregnant. However, this was rejected by many Companions and scholars (like Aisha, Ibn Umar, and Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib) because Fatimah's memory was questioned or her situation was exceptional. The Hanafi position: generally, a divorced woman has housing but not maintenance unless pregnant (based on the Quran and hadith of Fatimah bint Qays? Actually, the Hanafi school uses the hadith of Fatimah bint Qays as evidence that the thrice-divorced woman is not entitled to housing? No, the Hanafi position is that the divorced woman is entitled to housing but not maintenance; the hadith is used to support that. However, in this text, the dispute is presented to show that even a technically valid hadith may be set aside if the narrator is considered unreliable or the ruling is specific. The author uses this as an example for the conditions of accepting khabar al-adl.

Key Terms
السكنى (al-sukna): The right of a divorced woman to live in the marital home during the iddah period.
النفقة (al-nafaqa): Financial support for the divorced woman during iddah; Hanafi: only if pregnant.
المطلقة ثلاثاً (al-mutallaqa thalāthan): A woman who has been divorced three times (irrevocable divorce).
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A hadith transmitted by one or a few narrators, not reaching the level of tawatur.

Key Takeaway
A khabar al-wahid may be accepted but restricted to its specific context if supported by external evidence, preserving general legal principles.

Evaluating the Hadith on Zakat of Orphan's Property
Analyzing the ikhtilaf on zakat for orphan's wealth with hadith chain analysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Hanafi usul principles of hadith criticism (mursal, chain analysis) to evaluate the proof value of a disputed hadith.

Core Idea
A mursal hadith is not a proof in Hanafi usul, even if it appears to support an opponent's view.

The dispute over whether zakat is obligatory on an orphan's property hinges on a hadith: 'Seek good in the properties of orphans, lest zakat consume them.' Opponents use this to argue that if the property is invested, zakat is not due. But how sound is this hadith? In this lesson, we follow the classic Hanafi usul analysis that scrutinizes its chain of transmission. The conclusion is critical: the hadith is mursal and weak, and therefore cannot override the established practice of the Companions and general qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute and the opposing proof
Note the ruling in question: zakat on orphan's property. The opponent cites a hadith: 'Seek good...' to suggest that trading avoids zakat, implying non-obligation. Your task is to identify the exact wording of this proof in the passage.
The hadith is quoted in Arabic: 'ابتغوا في أموال اليتامى خيراً كى لا تأكلها الزكاة'.
2
Analyze the chain of transmission
Locate the author's chain analysis. He lists multiple narrations: from al-Shafi'i (mursal via Yusuf ibn Mahak), from al-Tirmidhi (via al-Muthanna, who is weak), from al-Daraqutni (via weak narrators). Identify which chains are marfu' and which are mawquf.
The only marfu' version is mursal; all other chains are mawquf (stops at a Companion) or have weak narrators.
3
Apply the Hanafi usul rule on mursal
The author states plainly: 'المرسل ليس بحجة عندهم' (the mursal is not a proof according to them). Understand that in Hanafi usul, a mursal hadith is not accepted as a binding proof (hujja) unless supported by other evidence.
This is a foundational principle: mursal is not hujja in Hanafi madhhab.
4
Evaluate the strength of the opposing proof
Combine the chain weakness and the mursal status: the hadith is not authentic enough to change the ruling. The author also notes that the mawquf narrations from Companions (Ibn Umar, Aisha, etc.) actually support the obligation of zakat.
The opponent's proof collapses under scrutiny.
5
Conclude the Hanafi position
With the hadith dismissed, the Hanafi position—that zakat is wajib on orphan's property—remains, based on the practice of the Companions and general principles (qiyas).
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is that guardians must pay zakat on orphan wealth that reaches nisab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك اختلفوا في زكاة الصبي، ولم يرجعوا إلى قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام ابتغوا في أموال اليتامى خيراً كى لا تأكلها الزكاة . أخرج ابن أبي شيبة عن ابن أبي ليلى أن علياً زكى أموال بني أبي رافع أيتام في حجره. وعن الزهري قال : قال عمر : ابتغوا لليتامى في أموالهم، لا تستغرقها الزكاة. وعن عبد الله بن دينار قال: دعي ابن عمر إلى مال يتيم، فقال: إن شئتم وَلِيتُه على أن أزكيه حولاً إلى حول. وعن القاسم قال : كنا أيتاماً في حجر عائشة، فكانت تزكي أموالنا. وأخرج عن ابن مسعود أنه كان يقول : أحص ما يجب في مال اليتيم من الزكاة، فإذا بلغ وأنس منه الرشد فأعلمه، فإن شاء زكاه، وإن شاء تركه. وأخرج البيهقي عن ابن عباس : ليس في مال اليتيم زكاة. وأخرجه الطحاوي في أحكام القرآن بلفظ : لا تجب على اليتيم زكاة حتى تجب عليه الصلاة. وقوله : ولم يرجعوا إلى قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام ابتغوا في أموال اليتامى خيراً كى لا تأكلها الزكاة : قلت : رواه الشافعي في مسنده عن عبد المجيد عن ابن جريج عن يوسف بن ماهَك أنه عليه أفضل الصلاة والسلام قال: «ابتغوا في أموال اليتامى لا تأكلها الزكاة». وهذا مرسل. وروى الترمذي من طريق المثنى بن الصباح عن عمرو بن شعيب عن أبيه عن جده أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : مَن وكي يتيماً : فليتجر له، ولا يتركه حتى تأكله الصدقة». وضعفه بالمثنى بن الصباح. وقال مهنا سألت أحمد عنه فقال : ليس بصحيح. ورواه الدارقطني من طريق مندل بن علي، وهو ضعيف، ومن طريق العرزمي، وهو ضعيف، ورواه ابن عدي من طريق الإفريقي، وهو ضعيف. وقال الدارقطني في العلل : رواه حسين المعلّم عن مكحول عن عمرو بن شعيب عن ابن المسيب عن عمر، ورواه ابن عيينة عن عمرو بن دينار عن عمرو بن شعيب عن عمر، ولم يذكر ابن المسيب، وهذا أصح. قلت : فآل الأمر إلى أنه الموقوف الذي أخرجه ابن أبي شيبة، ولم يبق في الباب مرفوع إلا مرسل ابن ماهَك والمرسل ليس بحجة عندهم، والله أعلم. فهذا انقطاع باطن معنوي أعرض عنه الخصم، وتمسك بظاهر الانقطاع، كما هو دأبه.
And likewise, they differed regarding the zakat of a minor, and they did not refer to his statement, peace be upon him: 'Seek good in the properties of orphans, lest zakat consume them.' Ibn Abi Shaybah narrated from Ibn Abi Layla that Ali gave zakat on the properties of the children of Abi Rafi', who were orphans under his guardianship. And from al-Zuhri: Umar said: 'Seek for the orphans in their properties, do not let zakat consume it all.' And from Abdullah ibn Dinar: Ibn Umar was called to the property of an orphan and he said: 'If you wish, I will take guardianship of it on the condition that I pay zakat on it year after year.' And from al-Qasim: We were orphans under the guardianship of Aisha, and she used to pay zakat on our properties. And from Ibn Masud: He used to say: 'Calculate what is due in the orphan's property of zakat, and when he reaches maturity and you perceive good judgment in him, inform him; if he wishes, he may pay zakat, and if he wishes, he may leave it.' And al-Bayhaqi narrated from Ibn Abbas: 'There is no zakat on the property of an orphan.' And al-Tahawi narrated it in Ahkam al-Quran with the wording: 'Zakat is not obligatory on an orphan until prayer becomes obligatory on him.' And his statement: 'And they did not refer to his saying, peace be upon him: Seek good in the properties of orphans, lest zakat consumes them': I say: al-Shafi'i narrated it in his Musnad from Abd al-Majid from Ibn Jurayj from Yusuf ibn Mahak that he, peace be upon him, said: 'Seek in the properties of orphans, lest zakat consumes them.' This is mursal. And al-Tirmidhi narrated via al-Muthanna ibn al-Sabbah from Amr ibn Shuayb from his father from his grandfather that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Whoever takes guardianship of an orphan should trade for him and not leave him until charity consumes him.' And he declared it weak due to al-Muthanna ibn al-Sabbah. And Mahna said: I asked Ahmad about it and he said: It is not authentic. And al-Daraqutni narrated it via Mandal ibn Ali, who is weak, and via al-Arzami, who is weak, and Ibn Adi narrated it via al-Ifriqi, who is weak. And al-Daraqutni said in al-Ilal: Husayn al-Muallim narrated it from Makhul from Amr ibn Shuayb from Ibn al-Musayyab from Umar; and Ibn Uyaynah narrated it from Amr ibn Dinar from Amr ibn Shuayb from Umar, without mentioning Ibn al-Musayyab, and this is more correct. I say: So the matter ends with it being the mawquf that Ibn Abi Shaybah narrated, and there remains in the chapter no marfu' except the mursal of Ibn Mahak, and the mursal is not a proof according to them, and Allah knows best. So this is a hidden internal disconnection that the opponent overlooked, and he clung to the apparent disconnection, as is his habit.
Source pages p. 402

Commentary
This passage is an analysis of a dispute (ikhtilaf) regarding whether zakat is obligatory on the property of an orphan (sabi). The author presents the arguments of early Hanafi scholars and the proofs they used. The text first demonstrates that many prominent Companions and Successors (Ali, Umar, Ibn Umar, Aisha, Ibn Masud) actively paid zakat on orphan properties, indicating their view that it is obligatory. In contrast, Ibn Abbas held that there is no zakat on an orphan's property. The author then addresses the hadith 'Seek good in the properties of orphans, lest zakat consumes them,' which opponents might use to argue that zakat is not obligatory if the property is invested. The author critically examines the chains of this hadith: one version is mursal (narrated by al-Shafi'i), another has a weak narrator (al-Muthanna). After analyzing the various transmissions, the author concludes that the only marfu' version is the mursal of Ibn Mahak, which is not considered a proof in Hanafi usul (since mursal is not accepted as hujja). Therefore, the hadith cannot override the practice of the Companions. The text ends by accusing the opponent of ignoring a hidden disconnection in the chain and focusing only on an apparent disconnection. The Hanafi position is that the hadith is not a valid proof, and thus the obligation of zakat on orphan property remains based on general principles and the practice of the early Muslims.

Key Terms
زكاة الصبي (zakāt al-ṣabī): Zakat on the property of a minor child.
مرسل (mursal): A hadith where the narrator omits the Companion and reports directly from the Prophet.
موقوف (mawqūf): A hadith that stops at a Companion, not attributed to the Prophet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because it is only narrated by one Companion.
D) Because it is abrogated.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a mursal hadith is not a valid proof, even when it appears to support a ruling; chain criticism is essential.

Hanafi Rules on Accepting Testimony and Narration from Sinners and Heretics
Explaining Hanafi rules on accepting testimony and narration from various categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi rules for accepting testimony (shahada) and narration (riwaya) from various categories of people and apply the criteria of reliability in each context.

Core Idea
Testimony from a sinner is accepted; narration from a heretic who invites to innovation is rejected.

This passage from Usul al-Bazdawi explains the nuanced Hanafi position on accepting legal testimony and hadith narration from individuals who are sinful, heretical, heedless, or negligent. The key distinction is that testimony in legal matters is treated differently from the transmission of prophetic traditions, because the latter requires a higher degree of trustworthiness due to the risk of fabrication in religious matters. By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Hanafi school classifies different types of people and the rationale behind accepting or rejecting their statements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories of people discussed
From the passage, list the various types: fasiq (sinner), kafir (disbeliever), child, insane, maghfal (extremely heedless), musahil (negligent), and sahib al-hawa (heretic). Note the distinguishing features of each.
2
Extract the ruling on testimony (shahada) for each category
State whether the Hanafi school accepts or rejects testimony from each category. For example, the fasiq's testimony is accepted; the kafir's, child's, and insane are rejected; the maghfal is rejected if habitually heedless; the sahib al-hawa is accepted except for the Khattabiyya sect.
The text also mentions those who claim ilham as not acceptable witnesses.
3
Extract the ruling on narration (riwaya) for each category
The passage only explicitly discusses narration for the sahib al-hawa: his narration is rejected if he calls people to his innovation. For others, the ruling can be inferred from the testimony ruling? Actually, the passage says the heretic is like the sinner in the matter of sunan (hadith), so the fasiq's narration might have a similar status? But the text focuses on the distinction.
The passage states that all imams agree on rejecting narration from a heretic who invites to innovation.
4
Understand the rationale behind the distinction
Why is testimony accepted from a fasiq but narration rejected from a heretic? The passage explains: testimony in people's rights (huquq al-nas) does not lead to falsification, whereas narration involves trust in conveying the Prophet's words, and calling to heresy tempts one to fabricate.
The heretic's depth in his doctrine restrains him from lying in testimony, but not in religious transmission.
5
Apply the distinction to new scenarios
Given a character description, decide whether to accept his testimony and/or narration based on the criteria. For example, a habitual gambler (fasiq) can witness a sale but cannot narrate hadith if he is also a heretic caller.
The neglectful person (musahil) is like the heedless if habitual; both are unreliable.

ألا يُرى أن الفاسق المسلم شاهد عندنا، بخلاف الصبي والكافر غير شاهد على المسلم أصلاً، فصار الصبي المسلم، والكافر البالغ في أمر الدين سواء، والفاسق فوقهما. حتى إنا نقول في خبره بنجاسة الماء : إذا وقع في قلبه أنه صادق تيمم من غير إراقة الماء، فإن أراق الماء: فهو أحوط للتيمم. وأما في خبر الكافر إذا وقع في قلب السامع صدقه بنجاسة الماء: توضأ به، ولم يتيمم فإن أراقه، ثم تيمم : فهو أفضل. وكذلك الصبي والمعتوه؛ لأن الذي يلي هذا العطف في كتاب الاستحسان الكافر، ففي رواية الحديث يجب أن يكون كذلك في حكم الاحتياط خاصة. - وأما المغفّل الشديد الغفلة : فمثل الصبي والمعتوه. فأما تهمة الغفلة فليست بشيء، ولا يخلو عامة البشر عن ضرب غفلة إذا كان عامة حاله التيقظ. - وأما المُساهل : فإنما نعني به المجازِفَ الذي لا يبالي من السهو والخطأ والتزوير، وهذا مثل المغفّل إذا اعتاد ذلك، فقد تكون العادة ألزمَ من الخلقة. وأما صاحب الهوى : فإن أصحابنا رحمهم الله عملوا بشهادتهم، إلا الخطابية، لأن صاحب الهوى وقع فيه؛ لتعمقه، وذلك يَصدُّه عن الكذب، فلم يصلح شبهةً وتهمةٌ إلا مَن تدين بتصديق المدعي إذا كان ينتحل بنحلته، فيتهم بالباطل والزور، مثل الخطابية. - وكذلك من قال بالإلهام إنه حجةٌ: يجب أن لا تجوز شهادته أيضاً. وأما في باب السنن : فإن المذهب المختار عندنا أن لا تُقبل روايةُ مَن انتحل الهوى والبدعة، ودعا الناس إليه. على هذا أئمةُ الفقه والحديث كلُّهم؛ لأن المحاجة والدعوة إلى الهوى سبب داع إلى التقول فلا يُؤتمن على حديث رسول الله عليه الصلاة والسلام. وليس كذلك الشهادة في حقوق الناس ؛ لأن ذلك لا يدعو إلى التزوير في ذلك الباب، فلم تُرَدَّ شهادته. فإذا صح هذا كان صاحب الهوى بمنزلة الفاسق في باب السنن والأحاديث، والله أعلم. وأما المرتبة الثالثة : باب بيان محل الخبر :
Do you not see that the Muslim sinner is a witness according to us, unlike the child and the disbeliever who are not witnesses over a Muslim at all. So the Muslim child and the adult disbeliever are equal in matters of religion, and the sinner is above them. Even to the extent that we say regarding his report of the impurity of water: if it occurs in his heart that he is truthful, he performs tayammum without pouring out the water; if he pours out the water, then it is more precautionary for tayammum. As for the report of the disbeliever, if the truthfulness of his report of the impurity of water occurs in the heart of the listener, he performs wudu with it and does not perform tayammum; if he pours it out and then performs tayammum, that is better. Likewise the child and the insane; because what follows this conjunction in the book of Istihsan is the disbeliever, so in the narration of hadith it must be likewise in the ruling of precaution specifically. As for the extremely heedless (maghfal), he is like the child and the insane. As for the suspicion of heedlessness, it is nothing, and the generality of human beings are not free from some heedlessness if their general state is vigilance. As for the negligent (musahil), we mean by him the reckless one who does not care about forgetfulness, error, and falsification; this is like the heedless if he becomes accustomed to that, for habit may be more binding than nature. As for the heretic (sahib al-hawa), our scholars (may Allah have mercy on them) acted upon their testimony, except the Khattabiyya, because the heretic falls into it due to his profundity, and that restrains him from lying, so it does not become a valid suspicion (shubha) and accusation except for one who is religiously obliged to believe the claimant if he adopts his sect, so he is accused of falsehood and fabrication, like the Khattabiyya. And likewise, whoever says that inspiration (ilham) is a proof, his testimony must also not be permitted. As for the matter of the sunan (hadith rulings), the chosen position according to us is that the narration of one who adopts heresy (hawa) and innovation (bid‘a) and calls people to it is not accepted. All the imams of fiqh and hadith are upon this; because argumentation and calling to heresy is a cause that leads to fabrication, so he is not trusted with the hadith of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). And it is not the same with testimony in matters of people's rights; because that does not lead to falsification in that matter, so his testimony is not rejected. When this is established, the heretic is like the sinner in the matter of the sunan and hadith, and Allah knows best. And as for the third level: the chapter on clarifying the place (mahall) of the report (khabar).
Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling from Hanafi usul on the acceptance of testimony (shahada) and hadith narration (riwaya) from various categories of people. The author begins by noting a fundamental distinction: a Muslim sinner (fasiq) is accepted as a witness in Hanafi law, unlike a child or a disbeliever, who are not considered witnesses over Muslims. This shows that the sinner is ranked above them in terms of testimony despite his sin. The author then applies this principle to a specific case: if a sinner reports that water is impure, the listener may perform tayammum if he believes the report, but he is not required to pour out the water. If he does pour it out, it is more precautionary. Conversely, if a disbeliever reports the same, and the listener believes him, he must still use the water for wudu and not perform tayammum; if he pours it out and does tayammum, that is better (but not required). This difference is based on the fact that the disbeliever's testimony is inherently unreliable in religious matters. The same ruling applies to a child and an insane person, since they are like the disbeliever in being legally incompetent. The author then discusses the extremely heedless (maghfal), equating him with the child and insane, and says that mere heedlessness is not a disqualifying suspicion unless it becomes habitual. The negligent (musahil) is defined as one who is reckless about errors and forgery, and if this becomes habitual, he is like the heedless. Regarding the heretic (sahib al-hawa), the Hanafi school generally accepts their testimony (except for the Khattabiyya sect) because their deep involvement in their doctrine restrains them from lying. However, if a person is known to blindly support anyone of his own sect, he is suspect. Also, those who claim ilham (inspiration) as a proof are not accepted as witnesses. In the context of hadith narration (sunan), the Hanafi position is stricter: narrations from heretics who invite others to their innovation are rejected. This is because narrating involves trust in conveying the Prophet's words, and calling to heresy tempts one to fabricate. This is unlike testimony in legal cases, which does not carry the same risk of forgery. Thus, in narrations, the heretic is treated like a sinner (whose testimony is accepted but whose narration is rejected in some views). The passage ends with a transition to the next topic: 'the third level: chapter on clarifying the place of the report.'

Key Terms
فاسق (fāsiq): A Muslim who commits major sins or persists in minor sins, but whose testimony is accepted in Hanafi law.
صاحب هوى (ṣāḥib al-hawā): A heretic, one who follows heretical doctrines (bid‘a) and may call others to it.
مغفل (mughaffal): An extremely heedless person who is often forgetful; treated like a child or insane in terms of unreliability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the Hanafi ruling on accepting the testimony of a heretic (sahib al-hawa)?
A) It is always rejected.
B) It is accepted, except for the Khattabiyya sect.
C) It is accepted only if he does not invite others to his heresy.
D) It is rejected because he is like a sinner.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school differentiates between testimony and narration: a heretic's testimony is accepted but his narration is rejected if he calls to innovation.

The Fifth Category: Conditions for Accepting a Fuduli's Report
Explaining the fifth category and the ikhtilaf on fuduli reports

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for accepting a fuduli's report in the fifth category and distinguish between Abu Hanifa's and the two companions' positions.

Core Idea
The fifth category's dual nature (binding rights and transactions) forces a middle path: either 'adalah or number for a fuduli's report.

In this lesson, we examine the fifth category of reports in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. This category includes matters like the dismissal of an agent or placement under guardianship. The key question is: what conditions must be met when a voluntary informant (fuduli) delivers such news? The answer differs between Abu Hanifa and his two companions, based on the nature of the information.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category and its examples
List the examples given in the passage: dismissal of an agent, placing a bankrupt under guardianship, dissolution of partnership/mudarabah, obligation of sharia rulings on a non-migrant Muslim, and a virgin's knowledge of her guardian's marriage. Understand that these are not pure transactions nor pure rights but a mix.
The category is defined by the type of legal consequences.
2
Distinguish between authorized and fuduli informant
If the informant is an agent or messenger designated to report, no 'adalah is required because they act as representatives. If a fuduli (uninvolved third party) reports, different rules apply. This is the core of the dispute.
The fuduli is not appointed; he volunteers the information.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's requirement
Abu Hanifa requires either a single upright person (one report with 'adalah) or two persons without the condition of uprightness. This is because the matter has aspects of both necessary rights (which require certainty) and transactions (which are more lenient).
The text says 'or two men' without specifying 'adalah, so number substitutes for uprightness.
4
Compare with the two companions' view
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider it purely transactional, so they accept reports from any two persons, regardless of 'adalah, including slaves, children, and women. The passage explains the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).
The two companions do not require 'adalah even in a single reporter if the number is two.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما القسم الخامس : فمثل عزل الوكيل، وحَجْرِ المأذون، ووقوع العلم بفسخ الشركة والمضاربة، ووجوب الشرائع على المسلم الذي لم يهاجر ووقوع العلم للبكر البالغة بإنكاح وليها إذا سكتت، ففي هذا كله إذا كان المبلغ وكيلاً أو رسولاً ممن إليه الإبلاغ: لم تشترط فيه العدالة؛ لأنه قائم مقام غيره. وإذا أخبره فضولي بنفسه مبتدئاً : فإن أبا حنيفة رحمه الله قال: لا يُقبل فيه إلا خبر الواحد العدل. وفي الاثنين: كذلك عند بعضهم. وقال بعضهم : لا تشترط العدالة في الاثنين. ولفظ «الكتاب في الاثنين محتمل، فإن محمداً رحمه الله قال: حتى يخبره رجل واحد عدل، أو رجلان، ولم تشترط العدالة فيهما نصاً. ويحتمل أن تُشترط سائر شرائط الشهادة، إلا العدد عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله، أو العددَ مع سائر الشرائط غير العدالة، فلا يقبل خبر العبد والصبي والمرأة. فأما عندهما : فإن الكل سواء؛ لأنه من باب المعاملات. ولكن أبا حنيفة رحمه الله قال : إنه من جنس الحقوق اللازمة من وجه ؛ لأنه يلزمه حكماً بالعزل والحجر، يلزمه (١) فيه العُهدة، من لزوم عقد، أو فساد عمل. ومن وجه يُشبه سائر المعاملات ؛ لأن الذي يفسخ : يتصرف في حقه، كما يتصرف فيه ،بالإطلاق، فشَرَطنا فيه العددَ، أو العدالة؛ لكونها بين منزلتين.
As for the fifth category: such as the dismissal of an agent, placing a bankrupt under guardianship, occurrence of knowledge of dissolution of partnership and mudarabah, obligation of the sharia rulings on the Muslim who did not migrate, and occurrence of knowledge of the adult virgin of her guardian's marriage arrangement if she remains silent. In all this, if the informant is an agent or messenger from one to whom reporting belongs, then uprightness is not required because he stands in place of others. And if a voluntary person (fuduli) informs by himself initially, then Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) said: Only the report of a single upright person is accepted in it. And regarding two, likewise according to some of them. And some of them said: Uprightness is not required in two. And the wording of the book regarding two is ambiguous, for Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) said: Until one upright man or two men informs him, and he did not stipulate uprightness in them explicitly. And it is possible that the rest of the conditions of testimony are required, except for number according to Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him), or number along with the rest of conditions other than uprightness, so the report of a slave, a boy, and a woman is not accepted. As for according to them (the two companions), then all are equal, because it is from the category of transactions. But Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) said: It is of the type of necessary rights in one respect, because it obligates him a ruling in dismissal and guardianship, it obligates him liability (al-uhdah) from the bindingness of a contract or the invalidation of an act. And in one respect it resembles other transactions, because the one who dissolves acts in his own right just as he acts in it absolutely. So we stipulated number or uprightness in it, because it is between two statuses.
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This passage defines the fifth category of reports: matters like the dismissal of an agent (azl al-wakeel), placing a bankrupt under guardianship (hajr al-ma'dhun), knowledge of dissolution of partnership or mudarabah, obligations on a Muslim who has not migrated, and a virgin's knowledge of her guardian's marriage arrangement if she remains silent. The ruling differs based on the informant: if the informant is an agent or messenger designated for reporting, then 'adalah is not required because they are representatives (qa'im maqam ghairihi). If a fuduli (voluntary uninvolved person) initiates the report, Abu Hanifa says only the report of a single upright person (khabar al-wahid al-adl) is accepted. For two reporters, some say the same (only if upright), and some say 'adalah is not required for two. Muhammad's text is ambiguous: he says 'one upright man or two men' without explicitly requiring 'adalah for the two. The passage then discusses whether all conditions of testimony except number (according to Abu Hanifa) or except both number and 'adalah are required, so that the report of a slave, child, or woman would not be accepted. In contrast, the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider all equal because it is from the category of transactions (mu'amalat) where 'adalah is not required. Abu Hanifa's rationale: these matters are of the type of necessary rights (huquq lazimah) in one respect (since they involve binding rulings like dismissal and guardianship, creating liability) and resemble ordinary transactions in another (the person dissolving acts in his own right). Hence, he required either number or 'adalah, as the matter lies between two categories.

Key Terms
فضولي (fuduli): A person who voluntarily reports information without being authorized or a party to the matter.
عزل الوكيل (azl al-wakeel): Dismissal of an agent; a report about such an event.
حجر المأذون (hajr al-ma'dhun): Placing a permitted person (e.g., a bankrupt slave) under legal guardianship.
العُهدة (al-uhdah): Liability or responsibility that arises from a binding contract or invalid act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the minimum requirement for accepting a report from a fuduli in the fifth category (e.g., dismissal of an agent)?
A) The report must come from at least two upright persons.
B) The report must come from at least one upright person, or from two persons without the condition of uprightness.
C) The report must come from a single upright person only.
D) Uprightness is not required at all.

Key Takeaway
The acceptance of a fuduli's report in the fifth category requires either 'adalah (one upright person) or number (two persons) according to Abu Hanifa, due to its dual nature.

Classification of Tazkiyah: A Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Dispute among Hanafi imams on tazkiyah's category

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding the classification of tazkiyah, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf of this difference.

Core Idea
Tazkiyah: Is it a condition of the narrator or of the report? Hanafi imams differ.

This passage explores a subtle but important disagreement among the three great Hanafi imams—Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani—regarding where tazkiyah (validation of a narrator's integrity) fits within the Hanafi classification of khabar. Understanding this difference refines your ability to analyze the conditions for accepting hadith reports.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two competing positions
State which imam places tazkiyah in the fourth category and which in the third.
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: fourth; Muhammad: third.
2
Understand the categories
Explain what each category concerns: fourth = conditions of narrator; third = conditions of report.
Tazkiyah is about narrator integrity, so it seems naturally a narrator condition.
3
Trace the thamarah al-khilaf
Consider how this classification affects the practical requirement of tazkiyah. For example, if it is a condition of the narrator, it must be verified individually for each narrator; if a condition of the report, it might relate to the overall reliability of the chain.
Both views ultimately require tazkiyah, but the conceptual framework differs.
4
Note that no tarjih is given
The text merely presents both views without preferring one. This is an unresolved intra-Hanafi difference.
Later Hanafi works may adopt one view for fatwa; this passage does not.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بخلاف المخبر إذا كان رسولاً؛ لما قلنا. وفي شرط الاثنين من غير عدالة على ما قاله بعض مشايخنا رحمهم الله فائدة لتوكيد الحجة، وللعدد تأثير في التوكيد بلا إشكال، والله أعلم. والتزكية من القسم الرابع عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف رحمهما الله ، وقال محمد رحمه الله هو من جنس القسم الثالث، على ما عرف، والله أعلم. معناه.
Unlike the reporter when he is a messenger, because we have said. And regarding the condition of two without integrity, as some of our teachers (may Allah have mercy on them) said, it is a benefit to strengthen the evidence, and number has an effect in strengthening without doubt, and Allah knows best. And tazkiyah (validation) is from the fourth category according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on them), and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) said it is from the third category, as is known, and Allah knows best. Its meaning.
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage presents a disagreement among Hanafi imams regarding the classification of tazkiyah, the process of validating a narrator's integrity. It begins by contrasting the case of a messenger, who merely conveys a message and does not require validation, with a reporter who witnesses the event. It then mentions that some scholars considered the requirement of two witnesses without established integrity as a means to strengthen evidence, emphasizing that number (multiplicity) does enhance certainty. The core issue is tazkiyah: according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, it belongs to the fourth category (al-qism al-rabi') of the divisions of khabar, which pertains to conditions of the narrator (such as 'adalah). Imam Muhammad, however, places it in the third category (al-qism al-thalith), which relates to conditions of the report itself. The phrase 'as is known' indicates this classification is based on prior established principles. The word 'معناه' likely begins a new subheading, but it is cut off here.

Key Terms
تزكية (tazkiyah): The process of validating a narrator's integrity ('adalah) in hadith transmission.
القسم الرابع (al-qism al-rabi'): The fourth category in the Hanafi division of types of khabar, concerning conditions of the narrator (such as 'adalah, tazkiyah).
القسم الثالث (al-qism al-thalith): The third category in the Hanafi division of khabar, concerning conditions of the report itself (such as chain continuity, lack of defect).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The classification of tazkiyah as a condition of the narrator (fourth category) or of the report (third category) reflects a subtle but meaningful difference in the structure of Hanafi usul.

Analyzing Conflicting Hadith on Writing: Prohibition and Permission in Hanafi Usul
Textual analysis of conflicting hadith on writing knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul methodology to reconcile conflicting hadith (ta'arud) on the permissibility of writing hadith.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school reconciles conflicting hadith by identifying abrogation or contextual specificity.

This passage presents the classical debate on writing hadith. As usul al-fiqh students, our task is not just to memorize positions but to understand how the Hanafi school weighs and harmonizes conflicting proofs. We will parse the evidence, apply Hanafi rules of conflict resolution, and derive the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting hadith
List the prohibition narrations (Zaid ibn Thabit, Abu Sa'id al-Khudri) and permission narrations (Abdullah ibn Amr, Abu Shah, Rafi' ibn Khadij, Anas).
2
Classify each dalil
Determine thubut (all ahad, zanni) and dalala (varying clarity). The prohibition hadith are explicit commands to refrain; the permission hadith include explicit commands to write.
The hadith of Abdullah ibn Amr has a clear imperative 'write'.
3
Apply Hanafi rule for ta'arud
When proofs conflict, first seek reconciliation (tawfiq). If impossible, check for naskh (abrogation) or tarjih (preponderance).
The author suggests reconciliation is easy, implying the prohibition was specific to early times.
4
Reconcile the evidence
The prohibition hadith were likely abrogated or context-specific (to prevent confusion during Quranic revelation). The permission narrations came later and are stronger in number and explicit command.
The Hanafi position holds that the permission was established by the Prophet's later actions.
5
Derive the ruling
Based on the preponderant evidence, writing hadith for preservation is permissible and encouraged.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
