وعن هارون بن عنترة عن أبيه عن ابن عباس : أنه رخص له أن يكتب ولم يكد. وحجة هذا ما رواه أبو داود عن المطلب بن عبد الله بن حنطب قال: دخل زيد بن ثابت إلى معاوية فسأله معاوية عن حديث فحدثه، فأمر معاوية إنساناً يكتبه، فقال زيد : أمرنا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أن لا نكتب شيئاً من حديثه، فمحاه. وما رواه مسلم عن أبي سعيد الخدري قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: لا تكتبوا عني غير القرآن ومَن كتب غير القرآن : فليمحه. وممن أجاز ذلك عمر بن الخطاب فروى عنه ابن أبي شيبة أنه قال: قيدوا العلم بالكتاب. وابن عباس : فروى عنه مثل لفظ عمر. والبراء، وأبو هريرة: روى ابن أبي شيبة عن عبد الله بن حنش قال: رأيتهم عند البراء يكتبون على أكفهم بالقصب. وعن بشير بن نَهِيك قال: كنت أكتب ما أسمعه من أبي هريرة، فلما أردت أن أفارقه أتيتُه بكتابي فقلت: هذا سمعته منك، قال: نعم. وعن معن قال: أخرج إلي عبد الرحمن بن عبد الله كتاباً، وحلف لي أنه خط أبيه بيده. وقد تقدم عنه أنه كره ذلك، والتوفيق فيه سهل. وحجة هذا ما روى أبو داود عن عبد الله بن عمرو قال : كنت أكتب كلّ شيء سمعته من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أريد حفظه فنهتني قريش قالوا: تكتب كل شيء ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بشر يتكلم في الرضا والغضب؟ فأمسكت عن الكتابة حتى ذكرت ذلك لرسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، فأومأ بإصبعه إلى فيه، وقال: اكتب، فوالذي نفسي بيده ما يخرج منه إلا حق. وما رواه الترمذي عن أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه قال: شكى رجل من الأنصار فقال : يا رسول الله ! إني أسمع منك الحديث فيعجبني ولا أحفظه، فقال: استعن بيمينك، وأومأ إلى الخط. للعلم ؛ لفقد العصمة عن النسيان. وهذا: باب الكتابة والخط: وما رواه عنه أيضاً قال: خطب النبيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فذكر قصة في الحديث ، فقال أبو شاه اكتبوا لي يا رسول الله، فقال صلى الله عليه وسلم: اكتبوا لأبي شاه. وما أخرج البخاري والترمذي عنه قال : ما كان في أصحاب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أكثر حديثاً عنه مني، إلا عبد الله بن عمرو ، فإنه كان يكتب ولم أكتب. وما رواه الطبراني عن رافع بن خدیج :قال قلت یا رسول الله ! إنا نسمع منك أشياء ،فنكتبها قال اكتبوا ولا حرج. وعن أنس بن مالك قال: شكى رجل إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم سوء الحفظ ، فقال : استعن بيمينك. وعنه : أنه قال : قيدوا العلم بالكتاب.
And from Harun ibn Antara from his father from Ibn Abbas: that he permitted him to write, and he barely did. The proof of this is what Abu Dawud narrated from al-Muttalib ibn Abdullah ibn Hantab: 'Zaid ibn Thabit entered upon Muawiya, and Muawiya asked him about a hadith, so he narrated it. Muawiya ordered a man to write it down. Zaid said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, commanded us not to write anything of his hadith, so he erased it.' And what Muslim narrated from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: 'The Messenger of Allah said: Do not write from me other than the Quran, and whoever writes other than the Quran, let him erase it.' And among those who permitted that was Umar ibn al-Khattab; Ibn Abi Shayba narrated from him that he said: 'Tie down knowledge with writing.' And Ibn Abbas: similar wording from Umar was narrated from him. And al-Bara and Abu Huraira: Ibn Abi Shayba narrated from Abdullah ibn Hanash: 'I saw them with al-Bara writing on their palms with reeds.' And from Bashir ibn Nahik: 'I used to write what I heard from Abu Huraira. When I wanted to leave him, I brought him my book and said: This is what I heard from you. He said: Yes.' And from Ma'n: 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Abdullah brought out a book to me and swore that it was his father's handwriting.' And it has already been mentioned that he disliked that, and reconciliation is easy. And the proof of this is what Abu Dawud narrated from Abdullah ibn Amr: 'I used to write everything I heard from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, intending to memorize it. Quraysh forbade me, saying: Do you write everything while the Messenger of Allah is a human who speaks in pleasure and anger? So I stopped writing until I mentioned that to the Messenger of Allah. He pointed to his mouth and said: Write, for by the One in whose hand is my soul, nothing comes out of it but truth.' And what al-Tirmidhi narrated from Abu Huraira: 'A man from the Ansar complained: O Messenger of Allah, I hear hadith from you and it pleases me but I do not remember it. He said: Seek help with your right hand, and pointed to writing.' For knowledge; due to lack of immunity from forgetfulness. And this: Chapter on writing and handwriting: And what was also narrated from him: 'The Prophet delivered a sermon and mentioned a story in the hadith, and Abu Shah said: Write for me, O Messenger of Allah. He said: Write for Abu Shah.' And what al-Bukhari and al-Tirmidhi narrated from him: 'There was no one among the Companions of the Messenger of Allah who had more hadith from him than I, except Abdullah ibn Amr, for he used to write and I did not.' And what al-Tabarani narrated from Rafi' ibn Khadij: 'I said: O Messenger of Allah, we hear things from you, so should we write them? He said: Write, and no harm.' And from Anas ibn Malik: 'A man complained to the Messenger of Allah about poor memory, so he said: Seek help with your right hand.' And from him: 'He said: Tie down knowledge with writing.'
Source pages p. 421

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of the debate regarding the permissibility of writing down hadith. The author presents evidence for both prohibition and permission. The prohibition evidence includes the hadith of Zaid ibn Thabit and Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, which forbid writing anything besides the Quran. The permission evidence includes actions and statements of Umar, Ibn Abbas, al-Bara, Abu Huraira, and explicit hadith like that of Abdullah ibn Amr and the incident of Abu Shah. The author then introduces a chapter on writing and handwriting, providing further permission narrations from Abu Shah, Abdullah ibn Amr, Rafi' ibn Khadij, and Anas. The Hanafi position favors permission based on these strong proofs, reconciling the prohibition as specific to the time of revelation to prevent confusion with the Quran.

Key Terms
الكتابة (al-kitābah): The act of writing down knowledge, specifically hadith
الحديث (al-ḥadīth): The sayings, actions, and approvals of Prophet Muhammad
العلم (al-ʿilm): Knowledge, particularly religious knowledge and hadith

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Conflicting hadith are reconciled in Hanafi usul by identifying abrogation, contextual specificity, or preponderance; the permission to write hadith is the relied-upon position.

Hanafi Rulings on Acting Upon Written Documents
Discussing the permissibility of acting upon discovered writings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify written documents according to Hanafi evidentiary rules, distinguish between known and unknown handwriting, and evaluate the role of istihsan in the ruling on documents.

Core Idea
Known handwriting is reliable; documents in opponent's hand are not, except by istihsan for ease.

Written documents (sukuk) present a challenge for evidentiary validity: can handwriting alone prove a claim? This passage from Usul al-Bazdawi outlines the Hanafi school's nuanced approach. It distinguishes between writings preserved with a trustee, documents in the hands of an adversary, and personal notes found in a known hand. The lesson also explores an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf where Imam Muhammad allows acting on documents by istihsan, expanding practical benefit.

Guided Path
1
Categorize the documents
Identify the four categories of writings discussed: writings with trustee, documents (sukuk) in opponent's hand, known handwriting (father/known person), unknown handwriting.
2
State the ruling for each category
For trustee: permissible like one's own; for sukuk: not permissible unless witness holds; for known handwriting: permissible to quote but not add; for unknown: alone invalid, with group and proper attribution valid like known.
3
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on sukuk
Note that Imam Muhammad permits acting on documents even if not in his hand, by istihsan, while the earlier view restricts to witness-held documents.
This is a legitimate difference within the school.
4
Analyze the istihsan reasoning
Understand that istihsan overrides strict analogy because error in handwriting is rare and to provide ease for people.
5
Apply the rule to a practical scenario
Given a scenario, decide if a document is actionable based on the categories and conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يُخاف عليه التبديل في غالب العادة، ويُؤْمَنُ فيه الغلط؛ لأن التبديل فيه غير متعارف. والمحفوظ بيد الأمين : مثل المحفوظ بيده. وأما في الصكوك فلا يحل العمل به؛ لأنه تحت يد الخصم، إلا أن : يكون في يد الشاهد. وكذلك قول محمد رحمه الله، إلا في الصكوك: فإنه جوز العمل به وإن لم يكن في يده؛ استحساناً ؛ توسعةً على الناس إذا أحاط علماً بأنه خطه ، ولم يلحقه شكٍّ وشبهة، لأن الغلط في الخط نادر. بقي فصل، وهو ما يجده بخط أبيه، أو خط رجل معروف، كتاب معروف فيجوز أن يقول : وجدتُ بخط أبي، أو بخط فلان، لا يزيد على هذا. فأما الخط المجهول فعلى وجهين: إما أن يكون مفرداً، وذلك باطل. وإما أن يكون مضموماً إلى جماعة لا يُتوهم التزوير في مثله، والنسبة تامة يقع بها التعريف فيكون كالمعروف، والله أعلم.
It is feared that alteration will occur commonly, and error is safe from it because alteration is not customary. And what is preserved with a trustee is like what is preserved with his own hand. As for documents (sukuk), it is not permissible to act upon them because they are under the hand of the opponent, unless the witness has it in his hand. Similarly, the statement of Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) except regarding documents: he permitted acting upon them even if not in his hand, by istihsan, as an expansion for people if he is certain that it is his handwriting and no doubt or suspicion occurs, because error in handwriting is rare. A remaining chapter: what a person finds in his father's handwriting, or the handwriting of a known person, or a known book, it is permissible for him to say: 'I found in my father's handwriting' or 'in So-and-so's handwriting', and he does not add to that. As for unknown handwriting, it is of two types: either it is alone, and that is invalid; or it is accompanied by a group in which forgery is not suspected, and the attribution is complete such that identification occurs, then it is like known handwriting. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the evidentiary value of written documents. It distinguishes between different situations: writings preserved with a trustee, documents (sukuk) in the hands of the opponent, and writings found in one's own or a known person's handwriting. The key principle is that while handwriting is considered reliable when certain conditions are met, documents (sukuk) are not generally acted upon unless in the witness's hand, except in the view of Imam Muhammad who permits it by istihsan for practical ease. Unknown handwriting alone has no authority, but if it is accompanied by a group and proper attribution, it can be treated as known. This shows the Hanafi approach to evidence: balancing strictness with practical concessions (istihsan).

Key Terms
خط معروف (khatt ma'ruf): Handwriting that is known and recognized as belonging to a particular person
خط مجهول (khatt majhul): Handwriting that is unknown and cannot be attributed to a specific person
صكوك (sukuk): Written documents, often legal or financial records
استحسان (istihsan): Juridical preference; departing from strict analogy for a more equitable ruling

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Permissible in all cases
B) Not permissible unless the witness has it
C) Permissible only if the handwriting is known
D) Permissible by istihsan always

Key Takeaway
Written documents are not automatically admissible; their evidentiary value depends on possession, certainty of attribution, and the possibility of tampering.

Linguistic Probability Remains Despite Narrator's Practice
Refuting the claim that a narrator's practice proves weakness in a hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a narrator's personal interpretation does not constitute jarh against a hadith, and apply the Hanafi usul principle that linguistic probability (ihtimal) is not nullified by individual practice.

Core Idea
A narrator's practice does not eliminate other valid meanings from a hadith — linguistic probability remains intact.

This lesson addresses a common argument in hadith criticism: that if a narrator acts on one interpretation of a hadith, the hadith is weakened. The Hanafi school firmly rejects this, establishing that linguistic possibility (ihtimal) is not erased by personal ijtihad. We will explore the principle and its application to three famous examples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opposing claim
Recognize the argument that a narrator's practice on one interpretation invalidates other possible meanings or proves hadith weakness.
This claim is often used to dismiss hadiths that have multiple plausible interpretations.
2
State the Hanafi counter-principle
The author asserts that linguistic probability (ihtimal) is not cancelled by a narrator's interpretation. Understand why this principle is foundational.
The principle is: 'احتمال الكلام لغة لا يبطل بتأويله' — linguistic possibility is not nullified by interpretation.
3
Examine the first example (Aisha and marriage)
Analyze how Aisha's action of marrying off her niece does not undermine the hadith 'no marriage without guardian'.
Her action was as a facilitator, not as a guardian, so it does not contradict the hadith.
4
Examine the second example (Ibn Umar and raising hands)
Mujahid's report that Ibn Umar did not raise hands except at the opening takbir only reflects Ibn Umar's practice, not a defect in the hadith about raising hands.
The hadith remains valid; Ibn Umar's practice is his own ijtihad.
5
Examine the third example (Ibn Umar and khiyar al-majlis)
The hadith about option of withdrawal has two possible meanings: separation by bodies or by words. Ibn Umar's interpretation of physical separation does not cancel the alternative meaning.
This is like ishtirak (homonymy), which is not eliminated by personal interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال: «أيما امرأة نكحت بغير إذن وليها فهو باطل»، ثم إنها زَوَّجت بنت أخيها عبدِ الرحمن وهو غائب، وكان ذلك بعد الرواية: فلم يبق حجةً. ومثل حديث عبد الله بن عمر رضي الله عنهما في رفع اليدين في الركوع: سقط برواية مجاهد أنه قال: صحبت عبد الله بن عمر عشر سنين، فلم أره يرفع يديه إلا في تكبيرة الافتتاح.
وأما عمل الراوي ببعض محتملاته: فرد لسائر الوجوه، لكنه لا يثبت الجرح بهذا؛ لأن احتمال الكلام لغةً: لا يبطل بتأويله.
وذلك مثل حديث ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما: «المتبايعان بالخيار ما لم يتفرقا»، وحَمَلَه على افتراق الأبدان والحديث يحتمل افتراق الأقوال، وهو بمعنى المشترك؛ لأنهما معنيان مختلفان والاشتراك لغةً لا يسقط بتأويله.
He said: 'Any woman who marries without the permission of her guardian, it is invalid.' Then she married off her brother's daughter, Abd al-Rahman, while he was absent, and that was after the narration: so it did not remain a proof. And similar is the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar, may Allah be pleased with them, about raising the hands in bowing: it fell due to the narration of Mujahid who said: I accompanied Abdullah ibn Umar for ten years, and I did not see him raise his hands except in the opening takbir. As for the narrator's acting on some of its possibilities: it is a rejection of all the other aspects, but it does not establish fault by this; because the linguistic possibility of the speech is not nullified by his interpretation. And that is like the hadith of Ibn Umar, may Allah be pleased with them: 'The two parties in a sale have the option as long as they have not separated.' He interpreted it as separation of bodies, while the hadith can also mean separation by words, and it is like a homonym because they are two different meanings, and homonymy in language is not cancelled by interpretation.
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific argument in hadith criticism: that if a narrator narrates a hadith but then acts on one particular interpretation, that proves the hadith is weak because it contradicts other possible meanings. The author refutes this, stating that a narrator's practice only indicates his own understanding, not that the hadith is defective. The key principle is that linguistic probability (ihtimal) remains intact; one person's interpretation does not eliminate other valid meanings. The author gives three examples. First, the hadith about a woman marrying without a guardian – Aisha narrated it but later acted in a way that seemed to contradict it, but the author explains her action was not as a guardian but as a facilitator. Second, Ibn Umar narrated the hadith about raising hands in prayer but did not practice raising except at the opening takbir; this does not weaken the hadith because his practice is just his personal interpretation. Third, the hadith about option of withdrawal (khiyar al-majlis): Ibn Umar interpreted 'separation' as physical parting, but the hadith can also mean separation by words; his interpretation does not cancel the other meaning. This is an important usul principle: the narrator's ijtihad does not constitute jarh against the hadith.

Key Terms
جرح (jarḥ): A defect that impairs the reliability of a narrator in hadith transmission.
احتمال (iḥtimāl): Linguistic possibility; a word or phrase having more than one plausible meaning.
اشتراك (ishtirāk): Polysemy; a single word having two or more distinct meanings (homonymy).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because linguistic possibility (ihtimal) remains and is not cancelled by personal interpretation.
C) Because the hadith is mutawatir and cannot be weakened.
D) Because the narrator's practice is irrelevant to hadith criticism.

Key Takeaway
A narrator's personal practice does not cancel linguistic possibilities; hadiths remain valid and open to multiple interpretations.

Companion's Departure from a Hadith: Not a Defect
Defense of companions' inaction on hadiths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a companion's departure from a hadith is not considered a defect (jarh) in Hanafi usul and apply this principle to similar cases.

Core Idea
A companion's inaction on a hadith does not weaken it; acceptable reasons preserve reliability.

In Hanafi usul, the reliability of a companion narrator is not automatically impugned if they do not act on a hadith they themselves transmitted. This lesson examines the principle through two classical examples: Ibn Mas'ud's preference for tatbiq over placing hands on knees, and Abu Musa al-Ash'ari's non-action on the hadith of wudu from laughter. Understanding this principle is crucial for properly weighing the Sunnah and avoiding unjustified rejection of authentic hadiths.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Recognize the implicit claim: a companion who fails to act on a hadith thereby introduces a defect (jarh) in the hadith's transmission or in his own reliability.
This objection is addressed in the text with the phrase 'if it is said'.
2
Analyze the Hanafi response to Ibn Mas'ud
Examine the reasoning: Ibn Mas'ud did not reject the hadith but considered it a rukhsah (license) and tatbiq as the 'azimah (stronger resolution). The preference for 'azimah does not invalidate the rukhsah.
The key distinction: departure is interpretative, not rejection.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to Abu Musa
Note the second reason: rarity of the event (laughter in prayer) allowed the hadith to remain hidden from the companion. This does not constitute jarh because the non-action is due to lack of awareness, not rejection.
The principle: non-action due to plausible excuse preserves integrity.
4
Derive the usul rule
From these examples, extract the rule: a companion's departure from a hadith, if accompanied by a valid reason (such as considering it rukhsah, or the hadith's rarity), does not constitute jarh. The hadith remains authoritative and the companion remains trustworthy.
This rule protects the Sunnah from being weakened by mere inaction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
علم أن القسمة من رسول الله عليه الصلاة والسلام لم تكن حتماً. وقال محمد بن سيرين رحمه الله في متعة النساء : هم شهدوا بها، وهم نَهَوا عنها، وما عن رأيهم رغبةٌ ، ولا في نُصحهم تُهَمَةٌ. فإن قيل: إن ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه لم يعمل بأخذ الرُّكَب، بل عمل بالتطبيق، ولم يوجب جرحاً. قلنا : لأنه لم يُنكر الوضع، لكنه رآه رخصة، ورأى التطبيق عزيمة، والعزيمة أولى، إلا أن ذلك رخصة إسقاط عندنا. ومثال القسم الآخر : ما روي عن أبي موسى الأشعري رضي الله عنه أنه لم يعمل بحديث الوضوء على من قهقه في الصلاة، ولم يكن ذلك جرحاً ؛ لأن ذلك من الحوادث النادرة، فاحتمل الخفاء.
Know that division (of spoils) from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, was not obligatory. And Muhammad ibn Sirin, may Allah have mercy on him, said regarding temporary marriage: They testified to it, and they forbade it, and we do not doubt their opinion nor suspect their advice. If it is said: Ibn Mas'ud, may Allah be pleased with him, did not act on placing hands on the knees, but rather practiced clasping the hands, and did not consider it a defect. We say: He did not deny the practice, but he considered it a license, and considered clasping the hands as the stronger resolution, and the stronger resolution is preferable, except that it is a license to drop it according to us. And an example of the other category: What is narrated from Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, may Allah be pleased with him, that he did not act on the hadith of ablution for one who laughs loudly in prayer, and that was not a defect, because that is among rare occurrences, so it allowed for concealment.
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage addresses the issue of companions not acting upon certain hadiths and whether that constitutes a defect (jarh) in their reliability. The author first notes that distribution of spoils by the Prophet was not obligatory, clarifying a principle of permissibility. Ibn Sirin's comment on temporary marriage (mut'ah) shows that early Muslims both witnessed its allowance and later forbade it, yet their opinions are not dismissed. The main argument responds to those who object that Ibn Mas'ud did not practice the placement of hands on knees in prayer (as per later practice) but instead clasped his hands between his thighs (tatbiq). The response explains that Ibn Mas'ud did not reject the hadith; he merely saw the other practice as a license (rukhsah) and tatbiq as the stronger resolution ('azimah), and the stronger is preferable, but he allowed dropping his own practice as a license. Similarly, Abu Musa al-Ash'ari did not act on the hadith regarding wudu from loud laughter in prayer because such laughter is rare, so the hadith remained hidden from him. Hence, not acting on a hadith due to an acceptable reason does not amount to jarh.

Key Terms
جرح (jarh): A defect or criticism that impairs a narrator's reliability in hadith transmission.
رخصة (rukhsah): A concession or license that permits an action normally prohibited or discouraged.
عزيمة ('azimah): The stronger, more cautionary ruling or practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Ibn Mas'ud practice tatbiq instead of placing hands on knees (akhdh al-rukab)?
A) He rejected the hadith.
B) He considered tatbiq the 'azimah (stronger resolution) and the other a rukhsah (license).
C) He forgot the hadith.
D) He preferred the opinion of another companion.

Key Takeaway
A companion's departure from a hadith due to considering it a license (rukhsah) or due to the hadith's rarity does not constitute a defect in the companion's reliability.

Mu'arada: Definition and Conditions
Defining mu'arada and its conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of mu'arada and identify whether an apparent contradiction meets its conditions.

Core Idea
Genuine contradiction requires two equally strong proofs at the same time and place.

Before resolving apparent contradictions, a Hanafi usuli must first verify whether a true mu'arada exists. This lesson unpacks the strict definition and conditions from the text, using the example of the donkey's leftover to illustrate how many apparent contradictions dissolve upon closer inspection.

Guided Path
1
Learn the definition
Read the definition from the source text: mu'arada is the confrontation of two proofs equally, with no merit of one over the other, in two rulings, with unity of time and place.
Word 'taqabul' implies equal strength.
2
Identify the conditions
Identify the three conditions: equal strength of proofs, unity of time, unity of place.
The passage adds 'in two rulings' as part of the definition.
3
Apply to the donkey example
Analyse the hadiths: one sahih (prohibition), one mudtarib (permission). They are not equal in strength, so mu'arada does not exist.
Also temporal factor: permission hadith is later.
4
Conclude
Conclude that many apparent contradictions are resolved at this stage without using the five methods of escape.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو تقديراً، ثم تحول رأيه، فصلى في ثوب آخر على تحري أن هذا طاهر، وأن الأول نجس لم يجز ما صلى في الثاني إلا أن يتيقن بطهارته؛ لأن التحري الأول أوجب الحكم بطهارة الأول، ونجاسة الثاني، وهذا وصف لا يقبل الانتقال من عين إلى عين فبطل العمل به. ومثال القسم الثاني من القسم الرابع: سؤر الحمار والبغل؛ لأن الدلائل لما تعارضت، ولم يصلح القياس شاهداً؛ لأنه لا يصلح لنصب باب المعارضة: قوله: لما تعارضت الدلائل: قال الشارح: فإن عبد الله بن أبي أوفى روى أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم حرم لحوم الحمر الأهلية يوم خيبر. وروى غالب بن أبجر أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أباح لحوم الحمر الأهلية. كان يكره التوضؤ بسؤر الحمار والبغل وابن عمر وابن عباس يقول: سؤره طاهر لا بأس به. قلت: حديث عبد الله بن أبي أوفى رواه البخاري في صحيحه، والإمام أحمد في مسنده. وحديث غالب بن أبجر رواه أبو داود. وأثر ابن عمر رواه ابن أبي شيبة. وأثر ابن عباس لم أقف عليه. ولقائل أن يقول: لا تعارض في هذا فقد قلتم: إن المعارضة: تقابل الحجتين على السواء، لا مزية لإحداهما على الأخرى في حكمين... إلى آخره، بشرط اتحاد الوقت والمحل... إلى آخره. وليس شيء من هذا موجوداً فيما نحن فيه، فحديث التحريم صحيح، وحديث الإباحة مضطرب، فلم يوجد ركن المعارضة. وحديث ابن أبجر متأخر، ففي لفظه: قلت يا رسول الله! أصابتنا السنة، يكن في مالي ما أطعم أهلي إلا سمان حُمُر، وإنك حرمت لحوم الحمر الأهلية؟ الحكم ابتداء: وجب تقرير الأصول. فقيل: إن الماء عُرف طاهراً، فلا يصير نجساً بالتعارض: فقلنا إن سؤر الحمار طاهر، وهو منصوص عليه في غير موضع. وكذلك عَرَقُه، ولبن الأتان، ولم يزل الحدث به عند التعارض، ووجب ضم التيمم إليه، فسمي مشكلاً؛ لما قلنا، لا أنه يُعنى به الجهل. وكذلك الجواب في الخنثى المشكل، وكذلك جوابهم في المفقود. ومثال ما قلنا من الفرق بين ما يحتمل المعارضة وبين ما لا يحتملها أيضاً: الطلاق والعتاق في محل مُبْهَم يوجب الاختيار؛ لأن وراء الإبهام محل يحتمل التصرف، فصلح الملك فيه دليلاً لولاية الاختيار، فإذا طلق عيناً، ثم نسي: لم يجز الخيار بالجهل. كيفية المَخلَص عن المعارضة: وإذا عرفت ركن المعارضة وشرطها وجب أن تبني عليه كيفية المَخلَص عن المعارضة على سبيل العدم من الأصل، وذلك خمسة أوجه: من قبل الحجة، ومن قبل الحكم، ومن قبل الحال، ومن قبل الزمان صريحاً، ومن قبل الزمان دلالةً. فقال: أطعم أهلك من سمين حُمُرك، فإنما حرَّمتُها من أجل جوالي القرية». فلم يوجد شرط المعارضة. تنزلنا، أليس فيه علة التحريم وهو كونها جلالة؟ ثم يقال: ما الموجب لترجيح التحريم في الأكل، وعدمه في السؤر؟ والله أعلم.
Or by estimation, then his opinion changed, so he prayed in another garment with the determination that this one is pure and the first is impure. His prayer in the second is not valid unless he is certain of its purity, because the first determination obligated the ruling of purity for the first and impurity for the second, and this is a description that does not transfer from one object to another, so acting upon it is invalid. An example of the second type of the fourth category: the leftover urine of the donkey and mule; because when the evidences contradicted, and analogy was not suitable as a witness, since it is not suitable for establishing ... The chapter of contradiction: His saying: when the evidences contradicted: The commentator said: Indeed, Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited the meat of domestic donkeys on the day of Khaybar. And Ghalib ibn Abjar narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) permitted the meat of domestic donkeys. And Ibn Umar and Ibn Abbas used to dislike performing wudu with the leftover of the donkey and mule, and Ibn Abbas said: his leftover is pure, no problem. I said: The hadith of Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa was narrated by Bukhari in his Sahih, and Imam Ahmad in his Musnad. The hadith of Ghalib ibn Abjar was narrated by Abu Dawud. The effect of Ibn Umar was narrated by Ibn Abi Shaybah. The effect of Ibn Abbas I could not find. And someone may say: There is no contradiction in this, because you have said: Contradiction is the confrontation of two proofs equally, with no merit of one over the other in two rulings... etc., with the condition of unity of time and place... etc. None of this exists in what we are discussing. The hadith of prohibition is authentic, and the hadith of permission is mudtarib, so the pillar of contradiction does not exist. And the hadith of Ibn Abjar is later, and in its wording: I said, O Messenger of Allah! The year of drought has affected us, I have nothing in my wealth to feed my family except fat donkeys, and you have prohibited the meat of domestic donkeys? The ruling initially: It was necessary to establish the principles. It was said: Water is known to be pure, so it does not become impure by contradiction. We said: The leftover of the donkey is pure, and it is explicitly stated in more than one place. Similarly his sweat, and the milk of the female donkey, and the ritual impurity is not removed by it at the time of contradiction, and it is obligatory to combine tayammum with it, so it is called mushkil (problematic) because of what we said, not that it is meant as ignorance. Similarly the answer regarding the ambiguous hermaphrodite, and similarly their answer regarding the missing person. And an example of what we said regarding the difference between what may bear contradiction and what may not also: divorce and manumission in an ambiguous place that necessitates choice, because behind the ambiguity there is a place that may bear disposition, so ownership is valid as evidence for the authority of choice. If he divorced a specific person, then forgot, choice is not permissible due to ignorance. The method of escape from contradiction: And if you have known the pillar of contradiction and its condition, it is necessary to build upon it the method of escape from contradiction in the manner of non-existence from the origin, and there are five ways: according to the proof, according to the ruling, according to the condition, according to the time explicitly, and according to the time by indication. So he said: Feed your family from your fat donkeys, for I only prohibited them because of the village roaming animals. Then the condition of contradiction did not exist. If we concede, is there not in it the cause of prohibition, which is that they are galla (animals that feed on impurities)? Then it is said: What necessitates preferring prohibition in eating, and its absence in the leftover? And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 453

Commentary
This passage from a commentary on al-Bazdawi's Usul discusses the concept of contradiction (mu'arada) and how to resolve it within the Hanafi framework. The author begins by illustrating a case where a person's initial determination of purity/impurity is contradicted by later evidence, leading to invalidation of the second prayer unless certainty is achieved. This sets the stage for the main example: the leftover (sür) of the donkey and mule. Here, contradictory hadiths exist — one prohibition of domestic donkey meat (narrated by Ibn Abi Awfa, authentic) and one permission (narrated by Ghalib ibn Abjar, weak and later in time). Additionally, companion reports (athar) from Ibn Umar and Ibn Abbas show differing practices. The author (likely the commentator) notes that there is no true contradiction because one hadith is authentic and the other is mudtarib (inconsistent), and also the later hadith includes a context that removes the apparent contradiction (prohibition due to them being galla — animals that feed on impurities). The Hanafi ruling is that the leftover of the donkey is pure (tahir), based on the principle that water is originally pure and that the permissible hadith (despite its weakness) is supported by the absence of clear evidence for impurity. The passage then extends this reasoning to the sweat and milk of the donkey, and draws an analogy to the cases of an ambiguous hermaphrodite (khuntha mushkil) and a missing person (mafqud), where certain rulings are suspended until clarity. Finally, the author outlines the five methods of resolving contradiction when it does exist: (1) considering the strength of the proof (hujja), (2) the ruling (hukm), (3) the condition (hal), (4) explicit temporal priority (zaman sarihan), and (5) implicit temporal indication (zaman dilalatan). These tools allow the mujtahid to determine which evidence to prefer without rejecting either entirely. The passage concludes with a rhetorical question: why is prohibition preferred for eating but not for the leftover? underscoring the nuanced application of usul principles.

Key Terms
المعارضة (al-muʿāraḍa): Confrontation of two proofs equally, with no merit of one over the other, in two rulings, with unity of time and place.
السؤر (al-suʿr): The leftover water or urine of an animal after drinking or from its body; here specifically the urine of donkey/mule.
الخنثى المشكل (al-khunthā al-mushkil): A hermaphrodite whose sex is ambiguous and cannot be determined, leading to suspended rulings.
المخلَص (al-mukhlass): The method of escape from contradiction by resolving which evidence to prefer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a required condition for mu'arada?
A) The two proofs must be of equal strength
B) The two proofs must be from the Quran and Sunnah respectively
C) The two proofs must apply to the same time
D) The two proofs must apply to the same place

Key Takeaway
Genuine mu'arada requires two equally strong proofs at the same time and place; many apparent contradictions dissolve upon checking these conditions.

The Donkey's Leftover: Resolving Apparent Contradiction
Resolving the apparent contradiction regarding the donkey's leftover

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi method to resolve apparent contradiction between hadiths on the ruling of the donkey's leftover (sür), and explain why it is considered pure.

Core Idea
The donkey's leftover is pure because the prohibition of its meat does not entail impurity of its leftover.

The most detailed example in the passage is the case of the donkey's leftover. Two hadiths seem to conflict: one prohibits donkey meat, the other permits it. Yet this is not a true mu'arada. This lesson walks through the Hanafi reasoning that upholds the purity of the leftover, and contrasts it with the Shafi'i position.

Guided Path
1
State the apparent contradiction
Two hadiths: one prohibiting domestic donkey meat, one permitting it. Also, companion reports show differing practices.
2
Check the conditions of mu'arada
Verify if the hadiths are equal in strength and same time/place. The prohibition hadith is sahih, the permission hadith is mudtarib and later, so no mu'arada.
Also the permission hadith includes a cause (jallala) that explains the prohibition.
3
Apply the principle of original purity
Water is originally pure. The burden of proof for impurity is not met. The permission hadith and companion statements support purity.
The text explicitly says: 'Water is known to be pure, so it does not become impure by contradiction.'
4
Identify the Hanafi ruling and proofs
The Hanafi position: sür of donkey is tahir. Proofs: original purity, explicit texts, and the permission hadith indicating overall purity.
The prohibition of meat is due to the specific cause of them eating impurities (gallā), not intrinsic impurity.
5
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
Shafi'i considers it najis based on qiyas on cats/wild animals and the implication of prohibited meat.
The text refutes this by distinguishing the cause.

Source Text
